Mid-Atlantic

Tragic Fire on American Mail Ship

Over Five Hundred Passengers Awaken from Dreams in Terror

Sixty Dead, Seventy-Three Missing

Sharks in the Sea Keep Company with Those Who Fall into the Water

(New York) The American ship "Morro Castle," weighing 11,600 tons, was en route from the capital of Cuba to New York when, in the early hours of today, it caught fire due to an electrical fault eight miles off the coast of New Jersey. The flames spread rapidly to the front and rear of the ship, prompting an urgent distress call via wireless telegraphy. Several ships received the signal and rushed to the scene to carry out a heroic rescue. According to a recent check, there were 558 passengers and crew members on board, of whom 425 were rescued. The death toll stands at 60, with 73 missing, far fewer than initially feared. When the fire broke out, most of the 318 passengers were asleep and unable to fully awaken, which is why many failed to escape. Furthermore, according to rescued crew members, many passengers were panicked by the flames and thick smoke and, despite the sailors' efforts to urge them into lifeboats, they were reluctant to leave the ship, resulting in their deaths. Miss Cabo de Villa, the daughter of the first Vice President of Cuba, was also among the passengers. Awakened by the shouting, she rushed out of her cabin only to be forced back by the flames. Fortunately, a sailor smashed a small window in her cabin, allowing her to crawl out through the opening. A fishing boat rescued one woman and seven men, but all died on the boat before they could reach land. The woman suddenly realized that the baby in her arms was dead and threw the child into the sea. Tragic events of this kind are too numerous to recount. Naval aircraft also assisted in the rescue, descending to pluck survivors from the water. According to crew members of one ship, they saw three sharks swimming among those struggling in the sea. Many of those rescued and brought here have been injured, but only with minor cuts and bruises. Some suffered nerve damage due to prolonged immersion in the water. (8th Reuters Telegram)

Asbury Park After the Morro Castle mail ship was destroyed by fire this morning, several ships are searching the coast of New Jersey in the hope of rescuing those who have not yet drowned. One hundred and eighty-three bodies have been recovered, and fifty are still missing, but there is little hope of finding any more survivors. The cause of the fire is believed to be an electrical fault caused by lightning. The total number of dead and missing is estimated at 230. Of the 558 people on board, 325 have now been accounted for. Bodies washed ashore all day, some burned beyond recognition, others drowned. Tax officers recovered 100 bodies. The British ship "Bermuda" rescued 72 people and brought them to New York. Some of them are in critical condition, while the rest are suffering from shock and cold and are in urgent need of medical attention. A small fishing boat rescued 70 injured passengers and recovered 10 bodies. The Morro Castle's lifeboat also brought 16 passengers and crew members ashore. The Customs Patrol boat "Danbury" rescued 15 crew members and towed the burned ship to New York. The Federal Steamboat Service has launched a detailed investigation into the incident. Some say the fire was not caused by an electrical fault. The ship was luxuriously equipped and operated between New York and Havana, Cuba, with a crew of 240 and 318 passengers at the time of the accident. The loss is estimated at US$3 million, all of which is insured. At the time of the accident, the ship was six miles off the coast of New Jersey when lightning struck, and within minutes the entire ship was engulfed in flames. At that time, the passengers were all asleep and had no time to wake up, resulting in chaos. According to the ship's deputy engineer, Mr. Pujo, the fire was so intense that the crew could not rescue the passengers, so they should not be blamed for dereliction of duty. Passengers, at a loss, jumped into the sea naked, but a few were able to swim six miles through the turbulent waves to reach the shore. (8th National Telegram)

Major Fire in Ishikawa Prefecture, Japan

Losses of Three Million Yen

Kanazawa A fire broke out in Daishoji Town, Ishikawa Prefecture, at 2:56 AM on the 9th. The wind was strong at the time, and the fire spread rapidly throughout the city. Zhongmachi, Daishin-dō, Nakakido, Banyang-chō, Hon-chō, Shinyashiki, Daishōji Promenade, Gotoku-chō, Nishi-Kannon-chō, and other major streets were completely reduced to ashes. All important organizations, banks, and companies have been destroyed. The fire brigade was unable to extinguish the fire due to its intensity. The Daishoji Police Department requested the Ninth Division Headquarters to send troops to fight the fire. The headquarters immediately issued an urgent order, dispatching two squads of engineer troops from Kanazawa to Daishoji at 8:40 AM this morning. As of 9:00 AM this morning, the fire has not subsided. (9th Japan United Press Telegram)

Kanazawa The major fire in Daishoji Town lasted for eight hours before being extinguished. The area is a center of the textile industry, with more than 50 factories. Today's fire destroyed more than 500 factories, government offices, companies, banks, and residential houses. 5,300 people are homeless, and the losses amount to 3 million yen. (9th Japan United Press Telegram)

American Labor Unrest Intensifies

135,000 People Join Strike

(Washington) The textile workers' strike intensified today, with another 135,000 workers ordered to join. Gorman, vice president of the United Textile Workers of America, ordered carpet workers to join the strike on Monday and 85,000 hosiery workers to join at midnight on Wednesday. The order was issued in response to some factory owners' plans to hire replacement workers and resume operations on Monday with police protection. Gorman suggested that both sides temporarily cease hostilities and wait for the mediation committee to make a public judgment, but warned that a tragedy could occur if management forced the factories to reopen. Although riots have gradually decreased in various places today, it is expected that they will recur if the factories attempt to reopen. President Roosevelt's special mediation committee is now doing its best to find a solution. Today, the committee consulted with AFL President Green for several hours in an attempt to find a basis for a public judgment. Green said that all issues had been discussed, but no practical solution had been found. Green is preparing to hold a meeting with union leaders in Washington next week to discuss the steps to be taken by workers in various industries to assist the textile workers. All AFL members who are working will contribute US$5 each to enable the textile workers to sustain a long-term strike. (8th National Telegram)

(Washington) The leaders of the hosiery industry union have decided that the number of people who will stop working due to the industry's strike will reach 85,000. At the same time, an independent union has also decided to strike, with about 4,000 members. Unorganized workers in the New England region will be affected. AFL President Green declared that he would contact the strike committee, but all unions affiliated with the AFL on Wednesday and Thursday have negotiated and decided on their attitude. It is generally believed that if the strike cannot be stopped, the unions will take serious decisions to maintain the strike. Gorman, chairman of the strike committee, has suggested to the mediation committee established by President Roosevelt that it should step in to arbitrate, but he has put forward three conditions: (1) employers and employees must be willing to accept the decision of the arbitration committee; (2) arbitration must be carried out by Monday at the latest; and (3) all spinning mills must be closed before the arbitration decision is made to prevent further killings. The employers have not yet responded to this matter. Gorman, chairman of the strike committee, stated in a published declaration that the strike is neither against the economic system nor against the government, but is a resistance to employers who are arrogant and disregard the intentions of the government. (8th Havas Telegram)

Japan's Diplomacy in Action Again

Ensuring Major Powers Understand Naval Policy

(Tokyo) Foreign Minister Hirota is now working hard to ensure that all parties concerned understand Japan's disarmament policy. It has recently been decided that Ambassador Saito to the United States, Ambassador Sato to France, and Ambassador Sugimura to Italy will return to their posts in early October to carry out their activities. Among them, Ambassador Sugimura will detour through London on his way to Italy to meet with Ambassador Matsudaira to the United Kingdom to discuss important matters. It is reported that Ambassador Matsudaira will return to Japan after the London Preparatory Conference to discuss countermeasures for next year's conference with the authorities.

Okada Resolves Issue of Garrison Organs in Manchuria

Military Demands Clash

Minister of War Hayashi to Resign

(Tokyo) Prime Minister Okada received Lieutenant General Nanjō, Chief of Staff of the Kwantung Army, at 1:00 PM on the 8th to hear the Kwantung Army's views on the issue of reforming the garrison organs in Manchuria. Prime Minister Okada intends to resolve the issue based on the following principles: (1) the military should be the center of the Manchurian administrative organs; (2) the military should also be the main body of the affiliated territories' administration. The demands of the Army authorities are: (1) general administrative matters of the Plenipotentiary Ambassador shall be supervised by the Prime Minister; (2) the first supervision of the Kwantung Army Governor shall be by the Plenipotentiary Ambassador and the second supervision shall be by the Prime Minister; (3) a Bureau of Manchurian Affairs shall be established with a military councillor as chairman; otherwise, no resolution will be recognized. Therefore, if Prime Minister Okada's resolution violates the principles of the Army, Minister of War Hayashi will resign. (9th Japan United Press Telegram)

American Financial Policy

Roosevelt Meets with Secretary of the Treasury and Others

Private Silver Imports to be Prohibited

Hyde Park President Roosevelt met today with Secretary of the Treasury Morgenthau, Budget Director Bell, and Chairman of the National Bank Perkins to discuss financial policy, which will be announced on Sunday. (8th National Telegram)

(New York) It is rumored that in order to effectively maintain the value of the dollar, the US Treasury Department may prohibit the import of privately owned silver. Market participants believe that such a ban will overturn the current plan for forward silver trading. (8th Reuters Telegram)

Tokyo Streetcar Strike

Police Department Determined to Mediate

(Tokyo) The Tokyo streetcar strike has been going on for five days, but the labor and management sides are still at odds. The Metropolitan Police Department is determined to mediate and summoned the strike committee secretary, Mr. Shimaue, at 11:00 AM this morning to issue a warning. (9th Japan United Press Telegram)

Chicago Municipal Government Distributes Back Pay

Queues to Receive Payment Stretch a Mile

Chicago Recently, Chicago received a loan of over 20 million yuan from the central government. This money has now been used to pay the back wages of municipal government employees and school teachers, who have not been paid for six months. All employees are eager to receive the money in order to pay off debts and purchase necessities. Therefore, they are happily queuing up to receive payment, with six people in each row, stretching about a quarter of a mile. (8th Reuters Telegram)

Page 10

French Foreign Minister Makes Contact for Two Days

Russia's Entry into the League of Nations Arrangement Completed

Two-Thirds Vote of the General Assembly Confirmed

Permanent Seat on the Executive Council Also Not a Problem

(Geneva) This evening, French Foreign Minister Barthou met with League of Nations Secretary-General Avenol and the Latvian Foreign Minister, and also consulted with Portuguese Foreign Minister de Mattos for a long time. De Mattos arrived here today from Paris with the Portuguese Chief Delegate to the League of Nations, Minister to France, Vasconcelos. As a result of French Foreign Minister's negotiations with representatives of various countries over the past two days, it seems that the legally required two-thirds majority in the General Assembly for the Soviet Union's entry into the League of Nations has been secured, and the number of votes obtained may be far above two-thirds. In addition, the granting of a permanent seat on the Executive Council to the Soviet Union requires unanimous approval by the Executive Council. At present, the countries on the Executive Council that have expressed opposition have voluntarily waived their right to vote. Therefore, unanimous approval within the Executive Council also seems to be not a problem. (8th Havas Telegram)

(Geneva) Polish Foreign Minister Beck held talks with British Representative Eden this afternoon. It is reported that Poland has requested France, Italy, and Britain to guarantee to automatically continue to elect Poland unanimously when the League of Nations Council is re-elected until Poland's non-permanent seat becomes a permanent seat. In this way, Poland may not oppose the Soviet Union's entry into the League of Nations. (8th Guomin News Agency Telegram)

Warsaw The semi-official Iskra News Agency declared that direct negotiations are currently underway between the Polish and Soviet governments regarding the Soviet Union's entry into the League of Nations. After reporting the above news, the news agency added comments. Judging from these comments, although the Polish government's final attitude cannot be predicted in advance, it will not take a firm and unyielding stance. (8th Havas Telegram)

(Geneva) It is now increasingly credible that Poland will not oppose the Soviet Union's entry into the League of Nations, and even will not oppose granting the Soviet Union a permanent seat on the Executive Council. Colonel Beck, the Polish Foreign Minister, requested in this morning's non-public meeting of the Executive Council that the Soviet Union's entry into the League of Nations be postponed for discussion until Sunday. And when Beck met with French Foreign Minister Barthou after the Executive Council meeting, he also made some expressions. At least from these two things, it can be proved that Poland has a tendency not to oppose it. According to the latest news, the attitudes of Argentina and Portugal are also no longer as firm as before. In short, judging from the situation tonight, it is by no means a dangerous speculation to say that the Soviet Union's entry into the League of Nations can obtain the approval of a very large majority in the General Assembly. Perhaps when the General Assembly votes, only Switzerland will remain opposed to the Soviet Union's entry, and most of the other countries opposed to the Soviet Union's entry have been persuaded to waive their right to vote at that time. (8th Havas Telegram)

Warsaw At the time of the League of Nations meeting, Poland again felt uneasy. According to the semi-official Polska Daily News, the entire Polish nation, regardless of party affiliation, is now watching the development of the League of Nations, and is even more apprehensive about the League of Nations' handling of the situation because the situation in Eastern Europe is precarious. Although Poland has repeatedly signed treaties with neighboring countries, it has not been enough to guarantee peace, and the treaties signed by Poland with its neighboring countries have not affected its previous alliances. For example, the non-aggression treaty signed by Poland with Soviet Russia does not affect Poland's alliance with Romania, and the non-aggression treaty between Poland and Germany does not affect the Franco-Polish alliance. However, these treaties related to the overall situation in Eastern Europe are now being shaken by other plans, and the concrete results that have been obtained are also in danger of being lost. Therefore, Polish Foreign Minister Beck's struggle in Geneva is supported by the entire Polish nation, etc. (8th Guomin Telegram)

Warsaw Admiral Galletti, commander of the Soviet Union's Baltic Fleet, sailed into Gdynia Harbor on the 3rd of this month with warships, formally visiting Poland, and set sail and left today, escorted to territorial waters by two Polish destroyers. Admiral Galletti and fifteen senior officers came to Warsaw and were cordially received by the military authorities. The sailors of each warship also visited the Poznań area. The government sent newspapers to repeatedly write articles stating that the visit of the Soviet fleet made the general friendship between Russia and Poland and the relationship between the two countries' navies even closer. (8th Havas Telegram)

Opening of the League of Nations General Assembly

(Geneva) The 15th session of the International League of Nations General Assembly is scheduled to open tomorrow. League of Nations Secretary-General Avenol will submit a report to the General Assembly. It has been learned that the report states that countries assuming mutual obligations, establishing mutual connections, publicly consulting, and abiding by customs are the entire system of the League of Nations. Once this system is destroyed, the entire world will inevitably be divided into several groups that are mutually hostile. If this is the case, the destruction of the entire world can be counted on the fingers. The report stated that since the last General Assembly, the League of Nations has undergone an important stage of crisis, but he has always had faith in the League of Nations, because although many of the hopes of the League of Nations' heyday have been delayed, the League of Nations is still urgently needed and indispensable for the modern world. Isn't this the reason why some large nations that have never joined the League of Nations now cooperate with the League of Nations more closely than before? The report continued to list the major issues to be resolved by the General Assembly. When describing the world economic situation, it stated that only international coordination can reverse the economic decline. This kind of international coordination can be carried out within the scope of a small number of groups at the beginning, and then gradually extended to the entire body. When describing the League of Nations system, it stated that the methods used by the League of Nations and its traditional practices are certainly not strict. It is certainly unnecessary to think that the League of Nations system is immutable, but it is also too early to change course immediately at present. (9th Havas Telegram)

(Geneva) British Foreign Minister Simon and Disarmament Conference Chairman Henderson have both arrived here. Henderson declared before leaving London that his trip was to inquire about the views of the various delegations on the current situation, and he had no intention of convening a meeting of the Disarmament Conference Presidium in the short term, because there are two important issues that should be resolved before the General Assembly: (1) the Soviet Union's entry into the League of Nations; (2) the Eastern European mutual assistance and non-aggression treaties. He does not believe that the Disarmament Conference can reconvene before the beginning of November. (9th Havas Telegram)

Agenda of the League of Nations General Assembly

(Geneva Correspondence) The 15th Annual General Assembly of the International League of Nations is scheduled to open at 10:00 AM on Monday, September 10, 1934. Its agenda has been compiled and translated as follows:

(1) Election of officers, appointment of committees, and approval of the General Assembly agenda:

(A) Appoint a Credentials Examination Committee and approve its report;

(B) Elect the President of the General Assembly;

(C) Approve the General Assembly agenda;

(D) Appoint the main committees of the General Assembly and allocate the items listed on the agenda to the various committees;

(E) Appoint the Agenda Committee;

(F) Elect the Vice Presidents of the General Assembly;

The items on the agenda are allocated to the following committees as usual:

First Committee Legal issues;

Second Committee Issues concerning the work of technical organizations;

Third Committee Issues concerning the reduction and limitation of armaments (this committee did not meet in 1933 because the Disarmament Conference was in session at the time);

Fourth Committee Budgetary and administrative issues;

Fifth Committee Social issues;

Sixth Committee Political issues;

(2) Report on the work of the League of Nations since the last General Assembly. The Secretary-General prepares a report on the work of the League of Nations since the last General Assembly every year. This report is published in two parts. One part is published in early July, describing the work up to mid-May, and the other part is published when the General Assembly opens. The above report is always the basis for general discussions at the General Assembly. The delegates have the opportunity to express their opinions on the work of the League of Nations at this time;

(3) Election of three non-permanent members of the Executive Council;

The resolution of September 15, 1926 (7th General Assembly) stipulates that three non-permanent members of the Executive Council shall be elected each year, with a term of office of three years from the date of election;

(4) Amendment of the League of Nations Covenant to conform to the Paris Pact;

On September 25, 1931 (12th General Assembly), the General Assembly discussed the First Committee's report on this issue and decided to establish a committee comprising representatives of all member states to seek unanimous agreement on the key points described in the report and to draft a final draft to be submitted to the General Assembly;

The Secretary-General was subsequently authorized by the Executive Council to agree on a date with the Chairman of the Disarmament Conference, the Chairman of the Executive Council, and the Rapporteur to convene the newly established committee, but this committee has not yet been convened. The reasons for this have been detailed in the supplementary report on the work of the League of Nations for the past year;

On September 25, 1933 (14th General Assembly), the General Assembly resolved to reserve this issue for discussion at the next annual General Assembly;

(5) The issue of cooperation in the news industry in the peace organization. A letter from the Spanish government reporting the proceedings of the Second Government News Agency and News Media Representatives Conference held in Madrid from November 7 to 11, 1933. On October 9, 1933 (14th General Assembly), the General Assembly convened the above conference at the suggestion of the Spanish government, paying special attention to examining the responses to the Secretary-General's question on "the dissemination of false information that threatens world peace and good understanding between nations." The General Assembly expressed the hope that the results obtained could be noted at the 15th General Assembly. The Spanish government's letter reporting these results was discussed by the Executive Council (78th meeting) on January 18, 1934. The Executive Council's report also stated that "the results of the Madrid Conference should be considered by the General Assembly, and the limits to which the League of Nations Secretariat can provide financial and administrative assistance should be decided;

(6) Various issues of the Nansen International Refugee Relief Bureau. In accordance with the Nansen International Refugee Relief Bureau's articles of incorporation, the League of Nations manages it in accordance with Article 24 of the Covenant and prepares an annual report on its work for submission to the General Assembly for review;

(Note: The Nansen International Refugee Relief Bureau is an international organization commemorating Dr. Nansen. Dr. Nansen worked tirelessly and made outstanding contributions to international refugee relief after the Great War, especially his relief of the Armenian people;)

(7) Regarding changes in the personnel of the various agencies appointed by the General Assembly;

A list of vacancies for all staff members of the various agencies appointed by the General Assembly will be distributed in the General Assembly for reference;

(8) Regarding various matters of the European Union Research Committee;

On September 27, 1933 (14th General Assembly), the General Assembly resolved to extend the term of office of the European Union Research Committee by twelve months;

(9) The Polish government's proposal to establish a general agreement on the protection of ethnic minorities;

The Polish government sent a letter to the League of Nations on April 10, 1934, requesting that its proposal to negotiate an agreement on the protection of ethnic minorities through an international conference be included in the General Assembly agenda;

(10) The audited accounts of the 15th fiscal year (1933) and the auditor's report;

In accordance with Article 38 of the League of Nations Financial Regulations, all revenue and expenditure accounts shall be finally approved by the General Assembly;

(11) The League of Nations budget proposal for the 17th fiscal year (1935);

In accordance with Chapter 4 of the Financial Regulations, the League of Nations budget proposal (including the Secretariat and special agencies, the International Labor Organization, and the Permanent International Court of Justice) shall be reported to the General Assembly for approval each year;

(12) Various reports of the Supervisory Committee;

In accordance with Article 16 of the Financial Regulations, the Supervisory Committee shall review the budget and prepare a report each year. Also, in accordance with the regulations, the Supervisory Committee's report shall also discuss accounting issues and all related issues arising from the decisions of other authorized bodies of the League of Nations. The Committee's report this year will also discuss the rationalization and centralization of the Secretariat and the International Labor Office, as this event was not finally included in the report to the last General Assembly;

(13) The issue of member states' arrears in contributions. On October 11, 1933 (14th General Assembly), the General Assembly resolved to request the Secretary-General to continue to find ways to recover the arrears in contributions from the member states and to report to the next General Assembly. The resolution also stated that the General Assembly believes that if there is no significant progress in this arrears issue within one year, the General Assembly will have to discuss a comprehensive solution to enable some member states to fulfill their financial obligations to the League of Nations;

(14) Report of the Management Committee of the League of Nations Staff Pension Fund;

In accordance with Article 20 of the Management Regulations of the Staff Pension Fund, the Management Committee shall prepare a report and submit it to the General Assembly for approval;

(15) Report of the Expenditure Distribution Committee;

On September 29, 1931 (12th General Assembly), the General Assembly decided to request the Executive Council to inform the Committee that it should submit a report again to the 1934 General Assembly;

I

Northwest Inspection Report 2

By our Special Correspondent, Geng Ya

Recent Conditions in Longxi Counties and Hami in Xinjiang Province (Continued)

Rural Bankruptcy: The tragic state of rural bankruptcy is even more difficult to describe exhaustively. Fields and gardens are desolate, lacking the resources to cultivate. Even selecting from among the relatively better-off farmers and compensating them for cattle and manpower to plant white opium, only to have them petition for the government to pay their land taxes, there are still none willing to take up the offer. Some eat only thin millet porridge, twice or even once a day. Some don't even get this one or two meals of thin millet porridge. Some have daughters aged thirteen or fourteen with no pants to wear, willing to offer them as child brides for a "one gold piece per year" bride price. (Wherever the car went, villagers flocked to see it. Those older girls without pants either bent over and sidled away or sat on the ground to watch from afar, their situation truly pitiable.) Some farmers from County A travel far to County B to sell their labor, while young men from County B come to County A seeking "hardship," drifting about with no fixed abode. The poem "Thousands of villages and tens of thousands of households are like the Cold Food Festival, with no smoke or fire to be seen, only flowers" is truly a portrait of today's rural Longxi. Examining the reasons for this situation, though the causes are numerous, the arbitrary apportioning of "unjust levies" on farmers by local bullies is a major fatal blow to rural bankruptcy. These so-called "unjust levies" are different from "excessive and miscellaneous taxes," and their harm is even more insidious and profound. To give an example, here are the four "unjust levies" imposed on Wang Youde, a farmer in the fourth district of Linze County's Weidipu, for ease of understanding: First, "Following orders, each household is required to provide four oil lamps, along with clean oil, and a lamp lighter for one day." Second, "Following orders, each household is required to contribute to the establishment of the district party headquarters, including photography and temporary transportation costs, the cost of meals and lodging for Committee Member Zhou of the High Court, and subsidies for the district militia commander, totaling four yuan, with a notation of four jiao on the account." Third, "Following official notice, each household is required to pay six yuan for miscellaneous expenses, postage, telegrams, printing, transportation costs, and local meals for the fifth district." Fourth, "Following public discussion of the Fairy Maiden Society, a ten-day opera performance will be held, with each household contributing twelve thousand cash coins and five catties of dried noodles."

Three Wonders Beyond the Pass: The "wind" of Anxi is extremely fierce. During the Qing Dynasty, a convoy of silver carts carrying military provisions to Xinjiang was once blown away, people and animals together. The reporter also encountered strong winds several times, with sand and gravel striking the car windows, making a frightening "clang" sound. Moreover, the wind-blown shifting sand can turn plains into hills and hills into plains, without a doubt. The "heat" of Turpan allows one to bury chicken eggs in the sand or stick slices of meat on rocks, and they will be cooked in a short time and ready to eat. The "cold" of Baliqiao (Zhenxi) still brings snow flurries in May and June, and winter urine freezes on the ground into ice. These are called the Three Wonders Beyond the Pass. Popular custom removes the two wonders of cold and heat in Xinjiang and replaces them with the women of Yumen and the scriptures of Dunhuang, which seems inappropriate. Also, here, just after the Autumn Equinox, the weather suddenly turns cool, and the locals are already wearing padded jackets, a climate not found in the southeast.

Rich Mineral Resources: Longxi is extremely rich in mineral resources. Those that naturally emerge on the ground and are repeatedly mined and abandoned include the gold mines of the Qilian Mountains in Zhangye and the Eight Great Gullies of Dunhuang, the coal mines of Changma, Honggou, and Beiyao in Yumen County, and the southern mountains of Jiuquan, Zhangye, and Linze Counties, and the oil fields of Chijinpu and Baiyanghe Village in Yumen County. The copper of Yumen, the lead of Jiuquan, and the salt lakes of Dunhuang and Haja'erzui are all substantial in terms of production and quality. Among them, the oil, after chemical testing, contains 15 to 17 percent gasoline components, making it a particularly valuable resource in modern times. Unfortunately, residents are only allowed to scoop it up for personal use, and no large-scale exploitation is done, so the gasoline used for aviation and automobiles here is purchased from distant Tianjin and Shanghai, with the value soaring eight or nine times higher (the price of each case of gasoline in Shanghai is eight or nine yuan, while here it costs eighty yuan), and that only includes the transportation costs and the loss from evaporation, not even the waste from damage. As the saying goes, "Begging for food with a golden bowl," this is precisely what is happening here.

News from Hami: Although Anxi borders Xinjiang and is the throat of transportation between Xinjiang and Gansu, because of the looting by ignorant Kazakhs between Qitai and Hami, transportation is blocked, so news from Dihua is rarely heard. Reports are conflicting and opinions are divided. Recently, postal letters have been able to get through, but packages are still not being sent, and telegrams are often sent but not received. According to a recent letter from Liu Yinglin, the administrative chief of Hami, to his friend Mr. Xia here, mentioning the recent situation in Hami, it can be used as a reference for the situation in Xinjiang Province. Here are some excerpts: "Hami Town is the gateway to the eastern route of Xinjiang. It has only now returned to our territory after being abandoned last year (referring to Ma Zhongying's occupation). After such a great calamity, recovery is not easy. Moreover, the price of silver notes has plummeted (four hundred taels of silver notes can only be exchanged for one yuan in cash), and the prices of all goods have soared, making it extremely difficult to maintain a livelihood. Currently, each hundred catties of flour costs fourteen or fifteen thousand taels of silver notes. The salary I (Liu speaking about himself) receive each month is only enough to buy one hundred catties of flour. Generally, those who do small errands and those whose livelihoods are difficult are fleeing, the situation is miserable, even worse than the great famine in Gansu Province in the eighteenth year [of the Republic, 1929]." After signing his name at the end of the letter, he added, "A disturbance occurred here in Hami (it is said that Sheng Shicai, along with Commander Xu from Dihua, led 500 soldiers, intending to station them in Hami, serving as the county magistrate of Hami, which was opposed by Yao Lebos, the leader of the Turban Muslims. Administrative Chief Liu was also under surveillance, but Xu's troops did not enter Hami City and soon retreated), which almost led to a war. Fortunately, the situation turned dangerous into safe and has now been restored to peace." Furthermore, according to people coming from Hami, recently Dr. Yao Lebos has called himself the Commander of Punitive Forces, and it seems that he will take action against the Dihua side, so the situation in Xinjiang Province is presenting an image of "an approaching storm." The future does not allow for optimism, and the central government should have already planned remedial measures. (Anxi, August 23rd)

Japanese to Reform Rehe Agriculture 3

Replace Soybeans and Sorghum with Opium

Rehe Correspondence: The Rehe Economic Survey Group, organized by the pseudo-Fengtian Railway Bureau, has recently completed its survey of Rehe's economic situation and natural resources and has decided to develop Rehe in the shortest possible time. The Chaore Railway built by the Japanese is currently being rushed to completion and will expand Huludao's "intake and output" to create an inseparable relationship with Rehe, in order to collect the effectiveness of transporting goods, and will increase troops along the Great Wall to control North China and approach eastern Chahar. According to the report of the survey group, the Japanese have also decided to reform Rehe's agricultural products, prohibit the planting of sorghum and soybeans, and replace them with cotton, tobacco, and opium. The income from the opium monopoly system will be used for military expenses and construction costs. Rehe's import and export trade volume this year has already made significant progress. Here are the trade volumes of Rehe Province from January to June of this year (unit: yuan):

Heavy Rain Causes Disaster in Luan County, Eastern Hebei

Water Four to Five Feet Deep in Tangshan and Luan County

People in Yutian Seek Refuge on High Ground

Tianjin Correspondence: Since autumn, there has been much rain in northern Hebei. The weather is overcast every day, and the temperature is already like mid-autumn. The amount of autumn rain in various places exceeds that of previous years. Tangshan, Luan County, Fengrun, and Yutian Counties suffered heavy disasters on the 3rd of this month due to heavy rain and sudden rise in river water. Details are recorded below:

Tangshan County: From September 2nd, the clouds were dense and there was drizzling rain. At about 2:00 AM on the 3rd, the rain suddenly turned into a downpour. In less than an hour, the streets were two or three feet deep in water. The Shuikou River of the Mining Bureau was flooded and overflowed, and traffic on all the streets and alleys was completely cut off. The eastbound No. 101 passenger train was delayed for two hours due to water accumulation on the tracks. Stores in all the low-lying streets and shops were flooded, and the goods were soaked, causing heavy losses. Hundreds of houses were flooded and collapsed here. At the same time, the Douhe River flooded and overflowed, and many farmlands and villages were flooded. Furniture and sundries floating on the water were countless. On the 4th, it was still not clear, and the entire city of Tangshan was still immersed in the floodwaters.

Luan County: For nearly half a month, mountain torrents have erupted upstream, and the water level has risen, flooding many farmlands on both banks. Traffic on the Luan River and long-distance buses has been cut off. On the morning of the 3rd, heavy rain fell again, non-stop all day. The water level rose again, and three sections of the upstream embankment were washed away. The water was six or seven feet away from the Luan River Railway. Seventeen or eight boats were sunk, and the villages along the river were all submerged. The water was four or five feet deep in the farmlands along the coast. Villagers who were flooded all climbed onto roofs or trees to escape the rain, leaving their belongings to be washed away. Vehicles traveling to and from Beining Road passed through the Luan River Railway Bridge with great care.

Fengrun County: On the night of the 3rd, there was a heavy downpour, and the water inside the city was about three feet deep. The main roads connecting the county with various places were all flooded. More than a thousand shops and households were submerged in the water. The water on both sides of the Douhe River and the coal transport river was turbulent, and the riverbed widened four or five times or more. Xuanzhuang and Lanzhuang were completely submerged due to their low-lying terrain. The county government specially requisitioned civilian ships to form temporary rescue teams to carry out relief work and telegraphed the provincial government to allocate funds for emergency relief.

Yutian County: On the 3rd of this month, due to strong winds and heavy rain, three breaches occurred in the Huanxiang River and two breaches occurred in the Jiyun River. Residents of villages along the river all fled to the high ground of Hongqiao Town. Two to three thousand people were living in makeshift sheds on the high ground. However, the weather was already cold at night, and cooking was difficult, causing many people to suffer from seasonal epidemics. County Magistrate Chen Baosheng has telegraphed the provincial government to request the allocation of funds for emergency relief. Recently, the water in Yutian City was also two or three feet deep, and traffic was blocked. In addition, Zunhua, Funing, Changli, and Qian'an Counties also suffered from flooding, but not as severely as the four places recorded above. (4th)

The Bandit Xiao

Attacks Lingling but is Repelled

Remaining Bandits Find it Difficult to Return to Their Lair

Guangzhou Correspondence: The various gangs of communist bandits Xiao Ke and Li Zongbao in southern Hunan recently attempted to break out of western Hunan and join forces with the bandit He Long on the Guizhou border. They were met and attacked by Hunan troops along multiple routes, and Guizhou troops were deployed to block them in Lingling. After the bandits were defeated and retreated, they avoided the strong and attacked the weak, mostly fleeing back to southern Hunan, Linwu and Lanshan. Recently, the bandit gangs have been unable to take advantage of gaps and are hesitating. On the night of the 31st of last month, bandits from Lanshan attempted to attack Yizhang, but were fiercely attacked by [unclear] troops. After about an hour of fighting, the bandits began to retreat to Xintian. At the moment, Hunan troops are advancing south step by step, so it is very difficult for the Xiao and Li bandits to break through. It is expected that the bandits will not dare to return to their old lair in the east. A telegram from the Hunan army yesterday reported the bandit situation as follows: "[Unclear] Secret: All of Xiao's bandits retreated successively to Yangming Mountain Huangbaijin on the night of the [27th]. Our [unclear] division followed up and attacked in places such as Fenshuiling, all with gains. Currently, they are confronting the bandits near Yong'anxu, which belongs to Xintian. According to Gui Xing, a surrendered puppet regiment commander, when the bandits' battle guards attacked, they used dense formations to pounce fiercely. If they were unsuccessful, they retreated. The bandits are very cunning. When the two armies are one or two days' journey apart, they only place unarmed soldiers and a small number of armed soldiers in their garrison to create a false appearance, while the main force, in plain clothes, takes advantage of the night to advance. Puppet party representatives hold great power. If three soldiers in the army are even heard speaking, they are brutally killed. A countermeasure seems to be to expand propaganda to undermine their morale and encourage them to reform. When fighting, adopt [unclear] formations, so that the bandits will have no way to use their cunning." It is specially heard that He Jian [unclear] (31st) printed (4th).

Anhui Province

Borrowed and Allocated Granary Grain for Famine Relief

Distributed to Severely Affected Counties for Price Stabilization

Anqing Correspondence: Anhui Province suffered a rare drought this summer, affecting more than forty counties, accounting for more than two-thirds of the province. The disaster-stricken people are clamoring for relief, but large-scale relief funds are difficult to raise in a short time. It is necessary to select the more severely affected counties and plan relief in advance. The Provincial Government's People's Food Regulation Committee now considers the grain stored in the Wanyi Granary in the provincial capital to be purchased with treasury funds and originally intended for famine relief. In the autumn of the 17th year of the Republic (1928), the provincial government originally resolved to allocate 80,000 yuan to the granary for grain purchase funds. Later, the Department of Finance only allocated 54,000 yuan due to the shortage of treasury funds. The granary currently has only 13,000 shi of grain in storage. Apart from the 4,000 shi that have already been selected and are being replaced by officials and gentry appointed by the Department of Civil Affairs and the Department of Finance, there are still 10,000 shi remaining. If all of it is allocated, it is feared that the provincial capital will lack food at times and will be unable to provide relief. For the sake of both, it is proposed to allocate 6,000 shi of grain from the granary, along with the 4,000 shi that have already been taken out for replacement, totaling 10,000 shi, and distribute it to the severely affected counties, ordering the county magistrates and sub-committees of the People's Food Regulation Committee to receive it and implement price stabilization or loan matters to provide relief. As for the amount of grain borrowed from the granary, the provincial treasury will allocate the same amount from the disaster relief reserve fund in the budget and purchase grain to fill the granary. This has already been signed and submitted to the provincial government for approval and instruction. It is expected that this measure of borrowing and allocating granary grain for price stabilization and famine relief will be approved. (September 7th)

The Bandits on the Anhui-Jiangxi Border

Are Gradually Collapsing

National Army Advances and Encircles

Major Destruction of the Bandit Nest in the Pseudo-Hexi County

Wuyuan Correspondence: The bandits entrenched in the Chengjiashan area on the Wuyuan-Qimen-Fuliang border area, although still resisting stubbornly and engaging in sporadic disturbances, are gradually collapsing due to insufficient internal strength and repeated setbacks, as the National Army continues to encircle and suppress them. At the moment, [unclear] regiments will join forces to suppress them within days. When the [unclear] regiment arrived at Xinghua Temple a few days ago, they killed a member of the pseudo-Hexi County Committee, a member of the district committee, and more than ten bandits, captured dozens of bandits, destroyed a pseudo-Hexi County Committee, a New Jiayuan arsenal, several clothing manufacturing plants, and a grain and fodder warehouse, with more than 30 dan of stored grain. According to the captured bandits, the bandits who fought with the [unclear] regiment this time were the pseudo-Vanguard Division, with more than a thousand people and seven or eight hundred guns. Another part was the pseudo-Guerrilla Force, with about seven or eight hundred people and more than four hundred guns. A few days ago, they had fled south from Wuguitou. The bandits who attacked Huangjian in Shexian County were also intercepted by the Beiding team there and retreated to the Hongguan Tuochuan Gaohu area in the ninth district of Wuyuan. Because the National Army was closely following them, they fled in disarray to Fuliang and southern Qimen. It is said that the bandits who harassed the sixth district attacked Jiadao Town (where the district office is located) the night before last, looted it, and then set fire to the Wanhe Cloth Shop and two umbrella shops before retreating along Yanqian Changxi Tianbaotang and other places. (4th)

Construction of the Nanjing-Wuhu Railway Begins

—Traffic will open in January next year—

Wuhu Correspondence: The Jiangnan Railway Company's construction of the Beijing-Zhao Railway, the first section from Wuhu to Xuancheng, has already opened to traffic, and passenger and freight transportation has begun. The second section, from Wuhu to Nanjing, has also officially started construction on August 25th after months of planning. The entire line is divided into four phases of construction: the first phase is from Wuhu to Daqiao Town in Dangtu County, the second phase is from Daqiao to Dangtu, the third phase is from Dangtu to Tongjing Town in Jiangning County, and the fourth phase is from Tongjing to Nanjing. The entire line is about one hundred kilometers long, employing 1,500 workers. It is planned to complete the earthwork and roadbed within two months. Eight hundred workers have already arrived in Wuhu, and the first phase of the project has already begun. The second, third, and fourth phases are also planned to start this month. The entire line is easier to construct than the first section from Wuhu to Xuancheng, as it mostly consists of flat land with no hills or high ground. The most substantial project is the Luqiao Bridge over the Dahe River in Dangtu. It is now planned to build a steel bridge, while iron bridges and wooden bridges will be built at other ditches and gaps. It has been decided that bridge construction and track laying will begin simultaneously after the earthwork and roadbed are completed. It is estimated that the entire section will be completed and open to traffic in January next year. The total cost of labor and materials is 5 million yuan. In addition, the thirty-li project at Sunjiabu, where the first section connects with the Xuanwu Line, is also being rushed to completion and can reach Sunjiabu directly from Wuhu within this month. (5th)

Fengxian: Adoptive Father Conspires to Sell Dry Daughter into Prostitution

Qianzhuang Pinjuan, a woman from Nanqiao, was conspired to be sold into prostitution by her adoptive father, Zhuang Boru, in collusion with Ni Shilin. After the County Women's Association reported the matter and requested an investigation, the county government scheduled several trials and pronounced a verdict in court yesterday. The kidnappers, Ni Baolin and Zhuang Boru, and the brothel keepers, Gu Wu and Liu Shen, were sentenced to imprisonment, and taken into custody separately. Also, Xu Linsheng, a county government clerk, impersonated a bailiff and helped the brothel keeper Gu Wu force Ms. Zhuang to return to Shanghai, which was also found to be true. He has been dismissed, and the Public Security Bureau has been ordered to expel Xu from the country to maintain public morals.

Suzhou: The Discharge Problem of the Dahua Factory Causes a Great Disturbance

The Dahua Paperboard Factory in Huguan Town has a capital of 500,000 yuan and is quite large in scale. Recently, the factory's illegal construction has caused opposition from citizens, and the Construction Department has ordered it to stop work. Furthermore, the factory has dug a river in front of the factory to discharge grass residue, causing the river water to become turbid and contain toxic substances. Citizens have sent letters to the factory requesting it to stop this practice to maintain the citizens' drinking water supply, but the factory has repeatedly delayed and continued to discharge as usual. As a result, the citizens were greatly alarmed. On the 7th of this month, citizens such as Chen Jianchou and Wu Xinzhi gathered the public and held a meeting at the district office, demanding that the district chief find a way to provide relief, and put forward conditions demanding that the Dahua Factory first use water boats to transport water every day to supply the citizens' drinking water, and then dig another river. Before another river is dug, the factory must suspend work for seven days to avoid further discharge of polluted water. District Chief Chen contacted the factory manager Zhang Deming, and the factory accepted the water transport but could not agree to the suspension of work, so the citizens were dissatisfied. At about 4:00 PM on the 8th, several hundred citizens gathered with incense at the sports ground and invited District Chief Chen to go to the factory to petition. District Chief Chen entered to negotiate at that time, and the citizens waited outside the door. Because the factory firmly refused to agree, the public was extremely angry and wanted to break into the door, but was stopped by the police. Wang Fangchen, a guard at the door, was beaten and injured by the public. However, because there were so many people, they were still crowded into the factory gate, with great momentum, and threw the incense they were holding into a pile of straw, and a fire immediately started, burning more than 24,000 dan of straw to ashes. The public then withdrew, and all the shops in the town closed. After the police district in charge reported to the Public Security Bureau, Inspector Zhang personally went to the countryside to conduct an on-site investigation in order to handle the matter. Those injured in this incident include Zhang Zhengyuan, Xu Shunquan, Zhu Jinwen, Jiang Yuankai, Xu Aliuyu and five others. In addition to sending a letter to the County Chamber of Commerce, the factory also telegraphed the Nanchang Headquarters and the Provincial Authorities, requesting a fair investigation and handling.

Theft and Kidnapping in Zhouzhuang Township

Lu Yikang, a farmer in Gaotianbang, Zhouzhuang Township, Suzhou, is relatively well-off. Bandits have coveted him for a long time. On the afternoon of the 8th, at about 1:00 PM, six bandits suddenly came, holding guns and pouring in, searching at will. They stole more than 200 yuan in silver and clothing. Before leaving, they kidnapped the owner, Lu Yikang, and left a note, demanding that the family prepare 5,000 yuan within three days for his ransom.

Promote Social Undertakings in Various Counties

Ma Yuanfang, the Director of Party Affairs in the First District of Jiangsu Province, convened a meeting of social education directors from various counties in Suzhou yesterday. Yao Qisu, Wang Chao-yi, Zhang Gengfu and seven others from Danyang, Zhenjiang, Kunshan, Wuxi, Wujin, Wujiang, and Wuxian Counties attended. The meeting was chaired by Ma Yuanfang, and the agenda included: (1) Determining the central work for each county in September; (2) The central work committee of each county should prepare a budget and submit it for approval; (3) Setting a deadline for submitting the status of social undertakings in each county; (4) This discussion meeting will be held once a month.

Wuxi: Autumn Cocoon Market Temporarily Suspends Opening

The Cocoon Industry Guild of this county held a general meeting of its members at 2:00 PM yesterday to discuss the opening date and cocoon prices for the autumn cocoon market, which is about to open. As a result, all members agreed that the Construction Department stipulated that each dan of dry cocoon in the autumn cocoon market would be charged six yuan for improvement fees. At a time when agriculture and commerce are in distress, our guild will never admit this and resolutely oppose it. We have previously submitted a request to the Construction Department of the Provincial Government for exemption, but we have not yet received an approval order. We should continue to telegraph the Provincial Department to urge approval. Before receiving the approval for exemption, there is no need to discuss the opening date and cocoon price for the cocoon market. After the discussion, the guild immediately sent a telegram to the Provincial Department, urging it to approve the exemption of the autumn cocoon improvement fee and quickly issue an approval.

Suicide by Taking Poison Due to Economic Pressure

Jiang Linshu, a resident of No. 58, Beilizhen, was engaged in the automobile business in Shanghai before, but has been unemployed for several years and has also become addicted to smoking, so he cannot make ends meet and is sitting idle. On the night of the day before yesterday (the 8th), he left his wife, Ms. Zhang, and went to the Dizang Temple on Xishan Mountain, where he secretly took poison. He died of poisoning at dawn. People called Ms. Zhang home to take care of the funeral. He left behind four or five children, which is quite pitiful.

Representatives from the Liyang Disaster Area Came to Wuxi to Beg for Relief

Liyang, a county located in the border area of Jiangsu Province to the west of this county, has been in a state of great loss of vitality since the great flood of the tenth year of the Republic (1921). Unexpectedly, this year it has suffered another severe drought, and the rivers, lakes, and dams have all dried up. The fields and crops in the whole county are withered. The business community is also unable to support itself and has closed down one after another. Disaster-stricken people have committed suicide due to lack of food and have fled to other places to beg for food. The fourth district of the county sent a representative to Wuxi to beg for relief. It is said that the local people in the county, seeing the severity of the disaster, are all extremely terrified. Therefore, they specially organized a Drought Relief Committee and appointed Shi Cantang and five others as representatives to beg for relief in the Wuxi-Suzhou-Shanghai area. Shi and others arrived in Wuxi yesterday and are scheduled to report the tragic drought conditions in the county to the party and government agencies, charitable organizations, and major philanthropists in this county this morning, and to beg for relief to benefit the dying disaster victims.

Changzhou

The Provincial Anti-Smoking Association Sends Personnel to Secretly Investigate Soil Merchants

Pan Youzhi, an investigator of the Provincial Anti-Smoking Association, had previously come to Changzhou to investigate the internal work of the County Anti-Smoking Committee and the anti-smoking situation in the county. It is said that Pan has recently come to Changzhou again in secret to investigate the smuggling of soil and the application of soil paste shops in various urban and rural areas. On the afternoon of the 8th, Pan visited County Magistrate Hou at the county government to discuss the anti-smoking issue in detail. He left after about an hour. It is also heard that he left Changzhou that night for Wuxi.

Jiangyin: Conflict Between Police Officer and Merchants

Liu Shihui, the patrol officer of the third police station of Yangshe Public Security Bureau, previously led the police to arrest Wang Ludeng and four other merchants from this town for playing mahjong and sentenced them to a fine of 14 yuan each. The merchants of the town felt that it was unfair to be fined such a large sum for playing mahjong and were dissatisfied. Three days later, the matter had not been resolved. Later, Guo, a person from the town, mediated and settled the matter for a total fine of 13 yuan. Unexpectedly, a few days ago (the 6th), four patrol officers were playing mahjong in a rice mill and were caught by Yang Shunbao and others. The mahjong tiles and other gambling tools were all taken to the Public Security Bureau. Patrol Officer Liu refused to accept the case. The patrol officers in the bureau used long benches and other weapons to beat Yang Shunbao and others. Now the local people are greatly angered and have reported the details of the incident to the General Bureau for investigation.

Jintan: The Disaster Situation is Extremely Severe and Relief is Urgently Needed

The disaster situation in Jiangsu Province is most severe in Jintan. After the severe drought, there was a pest infestation. Farming was abandoned and there was no way to salvage the situation. Local people have established a Drought Relief Association, and because the local economic capacity is limited, they have to beg for relief from philanthropists and charitable organizations across the country. Their public announcement said, "Since the flood of the twentieth year of the Republic [1931], Jintan has suffered from severe droughts in the twenty-first and twenty-second years, and has suffered from successive years of crop failure. Even if the harvest were bountiful, it would still be difficult to cope. Unexpectedly, there was little spring rain this year, and the bottom water was extremely shallow. In April and May, when it was time to transplant rice seedlings, there was no rain at all. Most of the highlands in the northeast, west, and south were not transplanted. The rivers near the water in the southern countryside were cut off and became barren land. In June and July, the drought was extremely severe. Even by the Autumn Equinox, the occasional light rain was of little help. The severity of the drought has not been seen in a century. Although the wheat harvest was considered moderate, the proceeds from the sale of wheat were used to purchase machinery to draw water in order to save the drought. However, when the machinery arrived, the rivers had already been cut off. The few cultivated fields that were planted were also withered. People changed to planting soybeans or buckwheat, but the heavens did not repent, and a pest infestation occurred, resembling crickets. The newly sprouted soybeans and buckwheat were also bitten off. The disaster area is vast and the days are long. The situation of holding food to feed others cannot be selected urgently. Public and private sectors are in distress and lack the ability to provide relief. We humbly request that philanthropists at home and abroad, the Chinese and foreign relief associations, the Shanghai Renji Charitable Hall, and various charitable organizations send personnel to conduct on-site inspections and provide relief. We are extremely eager to await orders."

Haimen: Qidong Residents Fear Food Shortages

Since the beginning of summer in Qidong, there has been a long drought with no rain, crops have withered, and the autumn harvest has been sharply reduced. According to a definite investigation, the total harvest in the county is 85,527 shi, and the total consumption is 1,577,527 shi, with a shortage of 1,492,000 shi. The lack of food for the people is very serious and is a serious problem at present.

Nantong: Bandits Harass Rural Areas

Recently, bandits have been harassing the four rural areas of Tongyi on a large scale. A robbery and injury to police officers occurred in Liuqiao. On the 8th, the county government ordered the security team to strictly guard against and investigate bandits and ordered them to solve the bandit case in the area within a week.

Yangzhou: The Anti-Smoking Association is Ordered to Reorganize

The Anti-Smoking Committee of this county was recently ordered by the provincial capital to reorganize and tighten its expenditures. Committee Chairman Ma followed the order and dismissed the chiefs of the various sections of the former committee, transferred Liu Fazeng, the secretary of the association, to concurrently serve as the chief of the general affairs section, transferred Dong Chengqi, the accounting director of the county government, to concurrently serve as the chief of the audit section, and transferred Zhang Shu, the director of the Public Security Bureau, to concurrently serve as the chief of the investigation section. As for the position of chief of the license section, it is still held by Chang Shizhi due to the heavy workload.

Japanese Warship Captain Visits Yangzhou

Morita Kazuo, the captain of the Japanese cruiser Uji, Nanjing Deputy Consul Aikako Nao Kyoko and others arrived in Yangzhou at 9:00 AM yesterday (the 8th) from Shanzhen on a private steamship to visit the scenic spots of Slender West Lake. The Public Security Bureau of the Provincial Capital specially sent a police officer to protect the wheel to Yangzhou. Upon receiving the news, the County Public Security Bureau also sent inspector Wang Lixin and others to supervise. After the sightseeing, they returned to Zhen on the same wheel in the afternoon.

Ningbo: Rice Shop Owner Shot Dead by Bandits

Wang Chunfu, a resident of Dantang, more than ten li outside Ximen, Yongbu, opened the Yisheng Rice Shop. At about 8:00 PM the night before last, six or seven bandits suddenly came and robbed all the current silver of more than 240 yuan earned that day. Seeing this, Wang immediately escaped from the back door and shouted for thieves. He was seen by a thief guarding the back door, who shot Wang in the vital point, killing him immediately. Wu Wenqing, Wang's sister-in-law, heard the noise and came out to see, and was stabbed in the right leg by the thief with a knife. Zhang Wenhe, a partner, was also beaten and injured by the thief. The thieves, having achieved their purpose, all rushed out the door and fled along the road.

Fishing Boat Encounters Robbery and Crew are Kidnapped

Wang Xianfang, a resident of Liangheng Township, Second District, Dinghai, makes a living by fishing and owns a large seine boat with several crew members. Unexpectedly, while the boat was fishing in the ocean a few days ago, it suddenly encountered a robber ship that ordered it to stop. More than ten robbers, all armed with sophisticated firearms, boarded the ship and kidnapped the crew members Wang Wencai, Wang Xianpin, Wang Xianxin, Wang Chengshan, Dong Lixiang, and the helmsman Dong Xiaolian. When they arrived in Chuanshan, the robbers took Wang Wencai and the other five ashore and abandoned the ship. In the midst of the chaos, Wang Wencai seized the opportunity to escape and immediately returned to Dinghai to report to the shipowner. The whereabouts of the other five are still unknown.

Xiaoshan: The Disaster Situation in Nansha is Dire

The disaster situation in Nansha, Xiaoshan, Xiaosibu, Heshanwu and other places is dire this time. The crops withered, and at the point of dying, they were fortunately revived by several inches of timely rain. However, they were followed by a pest infestation that ate the stems and leaves of soybeans, sorghum, and cotton, resulting in an average autumn harvest of less than 30%. The disaster situation is dire and has not been seen in sixty years. Therefore, in the past two days, villagers from various villages have petitioned the county government to submit the matter to the provincial government for exemption from taxes in order to relieve the people's difficulties.

Letter

To the editor: Regarding the news item in the local news column

Local News from This City 4

Yesterday

Anniversary of the First Uprising Led by the Premier

The Municipal Party Headquarters Convened a General Assembly in the Morning

Attended by Over a Hundred Representatives from Various Circles

According to the Central News Agency, September 9th is the anniversary of the first uprising led by Premier Sun of the Chinese Nationalist Party. The Municipal Party Headquarters convened the 39th anniversary memorial meeting of representatives from various circles in the grand auditorium at 10 a.m., presided over by Jiang Huaishu, Secretary-General of the Municipal Party Headquarters, who reported on the significance of the commemoration. The meeting adjourned at 11 a.m. The details are recorded below:

Order of the Assembly

(1) All stand at attention; (2) Sing the Party anthem; (3) Pay the highest respect to the Party and national flags and Premier's portrait; (4) The Chairman respectfully reads the Premier's will; (5) Silent tribute for three minutes; (6) Chairman's report; (7) Shout slogans; (8) Adjournment.

Representatives from Various Circles

The representatives attending from various circles included Chen Guoming of the Municipal Citizens' Association for Promoting Domestic Goods, Qiu Yuanming of the Land Bureau, Yang Derong of the Public Safety Bureau, Huang Zaoxiong of the Municipal Education Association, Mao Zeng of the Law Society, Gao Jie of the Second Senior Branch of the High Court, Lin Kecong of the Women's Association for Promoting Domestic Goods Movement, Wang Zongjian of the Jianghai Customs, Jiang Huaishu, Secretary-General of the Municipal Party Headquarters, Li Shiyong, Secretary of the Municipal Supervisory Committee, Huang Xianggu, Director of the Propaganda Department, and representatives from schools such as Junyi, Nongtan, Huiqiao, Zijin, He'an, and Shangwen, totaling over a hundred people.

Chairman's Report

After the ceremonial salutations, Chairman Jiang Huaishu gave a report, briefly stating: Today is the 39th anniversary of the first uprising led by the Premier. In this memorial meeting, we should first understand its historical outline. We all know that the Premier was from Cuiheng Village in Xiangshan, Guangdong, but the Premier's ancestry originated in Jinling. His distant ancestor, Duke Yuanzhong, served as the Privy Council Envoy during the reign of Emperor Shenzong of the Song Dynasty. Because his opinions on Wang Anshi's Green Sprout Policy went against the Emperor's wishes, he was demoted to Jiangxi, where he resided until his death. His fifteenth-generation ancestor, Duke Changde, was the Yuan Dynasty Prefect of Hangzhou, moved to Zhuji Lane, and later became friends with He Zhen, Duke of Wanbo. Together with his sons Gui Rong, Gui Hua, Gui Shao, and Gui Wu, he moved to Yuantoushan in Dongguan, which was the beginning of their arrival in Guangdong. By the Ming Dynasty, his thirteenth-generation ancestor, Duke Lizan, moved to Xiangshan County. The Premier's father, Duke Dacheng, engaged in agriculture in his early years. At the age of thirty-two, he married after ten years and gave birth to Duke Dezhang. From then on, the eldest daughter, Jin Xing, the second son, De You, and the second daughter, Miao Xi, were born three years apart. The eldest daughter and the second son died young. The Premier was born in the Bingyin year, also three years after the second daughter. After another five years, the youngest daughter, Qiu Qi, was born. When the Premier was born, Duke Dacheng was fifty-four years old, and Madam Yang was thirty-nine years old. This also shows the practical importance of eugenics in advocating late marriage. Since the Premier was a farmer's son, he was extremely clear about the suffering of farmers. In his youth, he aspired to alleviate the suffering of farmers. Later, he graduated from the American Education School in Honolulu and then studied at schools such as Royal College of Hawaii University, Guangzhou Boji Hospital, and Hong Kong Alice Memorial Hospital. He also obtained a doctorate. Later, he established a pharmacy in Macau and Guangzhou, where he began his revolutionary work and became acquainted with Zheng Shiliang, Lu Haodong, and Wei Youqin, gradually adopting a radical approach. At the age of twenty-eight, he wrote a letter to Li Hongzhang, which was not adopted, leading to the organization of the revolutionary group Xingzhonghui to call on revolutionary patriots to work together. By the time of the first uprising, the revolutionary atmosphere had permeated the country. China's achievements today are greatly influenced by the first uprising. We are commemorating this event here, and we should trace back the revolutionary spirit of the past and make it a model for our current revolutionary construction.

Slogans of the Assembly

(1) Strictly abide by the Premier's teachings; (2) Strive for the work of resisting Japan; (3) Strive to eliminate the Red bandits; (4) Unite sincerely to resist foreign aggression; (5) Revitalize the countryside and develop the Northwest; (6) Strive for construction work; (7) Long live the Three Principles of the People; (8) Long live the Chinese Nationalist Party; (9) Long live the Republic of China.

Johnson Arrived in Shanghai This Morning

Mayor Wu Hosted a Luncheon and Dinner Separately

The Belgian Envoy is Scheduled to Return Home by Ship Tonight

According to the Central News Agency, Baron Johnson, the special envoy sent by the new King of Belgium to China for notification and thanks, paid a visit to the Chairman of our National Government accompanied by the Belgian Minister to China, Ji Youmu, on the morning of the 8th to present his credentials. The Second Batch of Overseas Chinese Expelled from Japan

Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday

Arrived at 1 p.m. by the Tsukuba Maru

Our overseas Chinese compatriots in Japan have recently been unreasonably expelled by the Japanese. The first batch of fifty people returned home on the Japanese ship Kasado Maru on the 5th of this month. Thirty-one overseas Chinese who were forced to land in Moji returned home in two batches yesterday, arriving in Shanghai on the Japanese ship Tsukuba Maru and disembarking at Huishan Wharf at 1 p.m. Because the Public Safety Bureau had not received any notice beforehand, they did not send personnel to take care of the wharf. Only the first batch of expelled overseas Chinese went to welcome them. The details are attached below:

Arrived in Shanghai at Noon Yesterday, Extremely Embarrassed

The Tsukuba Maru entered the port at 11:30 a.m. and docked at the old Broadway Wharf at 1 p.m. The first batch of expelled overseas Chinese all went to the wharf to welcome them. These overseas Chinese were haggard, disheveled, and mostly had scars on their faces. They were extremely embarrassed and had a full of grief and wanted to cry but had no tears. After landing, they still stayed at the Daxin Gongzhan Inn in the Sixteenth Ward.

Detained in Moji and Severely Abused

A reporter from the National News Agency met with overseas Chinese Mr. Xia Yongchang on the ship. According to him, those who returned home this time were originally on the same ship as the first batch, but unexpectedly, when the ship passed Moji, they were forced to land by the Japanese water police. The overseas Chinese believed that since they had been expelled, they would not allow themselves to be subjected to such insults again, which angered the Japanese, who did not hesitate to take coercive action, handcuffed our compatriots, and tied them with rough hemp ropes, and beat them with fists and feet. We were all angry but dared not speak. What was even more hateful was that the Japanese water police burned the backs of our hands with cigarette butts and used short knives to cut a deep gash on the forehead of overseas Chinese Wu Linhao, causing blood to flow all over the ground. The cruelty of the situation is difficult to describe.

Presented to the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission Requesting Relief

Submitted to the effect of being unreasonably expelled and property confiscated, hoping that the government will approve serious negotiations to recover the industry, and use the national system to sympathize with the people. We have been doing business in Niigata, Japan, for many years, some opening Kori stores, some opening noodle shops, and some working as laborers. We have been following the rules and regulations and doing business peacefully. In recent years, the Kuomintang Party affairs in our country have developed abroad and are starting to set up branches directly under the Sendai branch. The number of people joining the Party has been increasing, which has been discriminated against by the Japanese. On August 10, 23rd year of the Republic of China, the Japanese authorities suddenly sent people to insult more than 70 of us and drive us back to the country, and did not allow us to carry our wives and children and property. We asked again and again, but they ignored it and escorted us to the Yokohama Consulate for more than ten days. Our Consul General Wang Hongnian sent representatives to the Japan Mail Ship Company and contacted the Kasado Maru, and then bought group tickets on the 27th at 11 a.m. Captain Yokoyama was responsible for protecting us along the way. We landed in Shanghai. On September 1st, the ship arrived in Moji, and after entering the port, water police came to check the ship. They said that there were too many people and were not allowed to return home together. We discussed it with them, and they relied on violence to beat us and did not allow us to say a word. They also mobilized more than 100 ground police teams, gathered in the ship, tied us more than 80 people with hemp ropes, and scolded and beat us at the same time. Zhou Baozhen wanted to beg them a few words, but the police were like jackals and wolves, and they pushed Zhou into the sea. Fortunately, we tried our best to rescue him and saved his life. Wu Linhao was chased on the deck and was seriously injured by a gun butt. His waist was stabbed by a bayonet to a depth of about two inches. We saw that he was so fierce and did not dare to resist him, so we had to let him arrange it. They then ordered us to divide into two groups. The first group of 50 people took the Kasado Maru back to China first, and the second group was detained at the Moji police station to wait for another ship. The next day, they ordered us to send representatives Chen Fengqing and beat our fingerprints on white paper before releasing us 50 people to board the ship. The Kasado Maru arrived in Shanghai on the same day. We were bullied and abused along the way and suffered unspeakable hardships. The remaining 30 people are still being held in Moji, and their lives and deaths are uncertain. I think that our dignified China is now being arbitrarily trampled by the brutal Japanese slaves. Anyone with a little bit of blood boils when they hear it. The loss of money to us is a small matter, but the loss of national prestige is a big matter. For this reason, we implore you to provide assistance, send personnel to Beijing to petition, negotiate seriously, compensate for the loss, and recover all the property that we accumulated in Japan with our blood and sweat, so that we can find another way to live. The country will be fortunate, the overseas Chinese will be fortunate, and we will be grateful. In addition to sending letters to various organizations to request assistance, we have prepared a document to request you to implement it quickly, which is a virtue.

Names of the Third Batch of Expelled Refugees

Pan Jinkai, Pan Lianbao, Chen Hesheng, Chen Guozhen, Hu Jiaqi, Zhou Chengshan, Zhou Chengkun, Zhou Junkun, Ye Zhichao, Lin Tuizong, Huang Peiliang, Pan Yaoming, Yang Zhankong, Xia Yongchang, Qian Qinsheng, etc., a total of 15 people.

Names of Overseas Chinese Detained in Moji

Ye Jinshun, Pan Rishun, Zhou Yishun, Dai Changtao, Zhou Rixin, Chen Yangao, Zhou Baozhen, Ji Zhongchang, Wang Jinbao, Wu Linhao, Pan Yichuan, Hu Jiada, Hu Zida, a total of 13 people.

The Nanjing Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission previously sent Tan Zhonglu and Li Zhujian to Shanghai to express condolences. Yesterday, they also received a telegram notifying Tan et al. that temporary relief funds of five yuan per person would be issued temporarily, and the funds would be remitted to Shanghai. As for whether to send them back to their original places or find other appropriate ways to provide relief, it is still unknown.
