Shen Bao Medical and Pharmaceutical Weekly

Further Explications on Typhoid Fever 4 (Taiyang) (Middle) 20

— Yu Yunxiu

To interpret it forcibly: "Wind injures the 'ying'" refers to various airborne infectious diseases of today. Wind itself cannot cause disease; the disease caused by wind is due to the impurities it carries. Song Yu's "Ode to Wind" states, "The wind of commoners rises from poor alleys, stirring dust and creating oppressive resentment. It assaults doors and windows, moving sand and ashes, frightening filth, and scattering rottenness. Insidiously entering through broken windows, it reaches dwellings. Therefore, the condition of those affected by this wind is confused, depressed, and distressed, causing warmth and dampness, with deep sadness in their hearts, generating illness and heat, with sores on their lips and shadows on their eyes." Yu Hangzhang believes that wind causes disease precisely by frightening filth and scattering rottenness, allowing pathogenic microorganisms to fly in the air and sow themselves in the human body. This can be said to reveal the hidden nature of wind. The one who speaks well of the ancients must have verifications in the present. Since there are pathogenic microorganisms in the air, flying objects enter the human body, either inhaled through the mouth and nose or attached to broken skin, then mixing into tissue cell fluid. It enters the blood through the lymphatic vessels to form various diseases, such as scarlet fever, measles, chickenpox, and influenza. In that case, the pathogens of airborne infectious diseases mostly enter the blood through the lymphatic medium. Considering this as "wind injures the 'wei'" is not impossible. However, when the disease occurs, it is because the pathogens multiply in the blood, producing toxins that lead to illness, which should no longer be considered a lymphatic disease. The symptoms vary depending on the individual characteristics of the disease contracted, and the treatment also varies depending on what the disease harms. How can one prescribe cinnamon twig decoction for "wind injures the 'wei'" as one of the three cardinal principles?

From the above, it is known that "cold injures the 'ying'" is not the "typhoid fever" in the "Taiyang" chapter of "Treatise on Cold Damage Diseases," and "wind injures the 'wei'" is not the "wind stroke" with cinnamon twig decoction. Therefore, the so-called "wind and cold both injure the 'ying' and 'wei'" in the third cardinal principle cannot be established at all. The absurdity is self-evident.

Some people in the past also knew that the theory of the three cardinal principles was wrong. Ke Yunbo did. He replaced the names "wind injures the 'wei' and cold injures the 'ying'" with "cinnamon twig decoction syndrome" and "ephedra decoction syndrome." This method is based on Sun Simiao's "Thousand Gold Wings" using the method of cinnamon twig decoction and the method of ephedra decoction, and Xu Lingtai's "Formulae Classified According to 'Treatise on Cold Damage Diseases'" develops and changes it to the extreme. Xu's preface to "Formulae Classified According to 'Treatise on Cold Damage Diseases'" says, "The 'Treatise on Cold Damage Diseases' did not exist as a complete book at the time; it was collected by Wang Shuhe. Although it is divided into six meridians, the language has no order. Yang meridians often have Yin meridian treatments, and Yin meridians often have Yang meridian treatments." It also says, "At that time, books were written by prescribing based on symptoms, with no fixed order." I think this is very true. The book by Zhang Zhongjing is a prescription case from that time. Treatment does not necessarily involve one person, and prescriptions are not fixed at one time. Prescriptions are based on symptoms and location. Even if they are not all from Zhang Zhongjing's hand, they are also, as mentioned in the preface, "widely collected from various prescriptions." These are prescription cases from the ancients. Treatment does not necessarily involve one person, and prescriptions are not fixed at one time. Prescriptions are also based on symptoms and location. Later scholars did not understand this meaning and reversed it, disordered it, changed the order, distinguished the true from the false, and strived to connect the top and bottom, linking them into one breath to develop a special system. This is the "Treatise on Cold Damage Diseases" of later generations, not the "Treatise on Cold Damage Diseases" of Zhang Zhongjing. To think that one can obtain the original face of Zhang Zhongjing's text is not too far-fetched. From Fang Zhonghang downwards, they are busy and tireless, truly what is called "a fool troubles himself."

In addition to the three cardinal principles in the "Taiyang" chapter, the most debated by various schools is the cinnamon twig decoction. Since ancient times, doctors have said that Zhang Zhongjing's method is to use cinnamon twig decoction for those with sweat and ephedra decoction for those without sweat. Moreover, because the "Treatise on Cold Damage Diseases" says, "Cinnamon twig is originally for resolving the muscles. If the person's pulse is floating and tense, has fever, and does not sweat, it should not be given." Therefore, it is said that the method of "sipping hot rice porridge and covering warmly to induce a slight sweat all over the body" with cinnamon twig decoction is the method of cinnamon twig for resolving the muscles, and that resolving the muscles is exclusively attributed to cinnamon twig. Xu Huixi, known as being able to read ancient books, also held this view. What else can the rest say? Shen Shi's "Ephedra Muscle Resolving Decoction" is found in "Waike Secret Records," Volume 1. Its four ingredients, dosage, decoction method, and administration method are all the same as Zhang Zhongjing's ephedra decoction, only the cinnamon twig is replaced with cinnamon heart. Moreover, there is a note at the end saying, "Based on Zhang Zhongjing's Ephedra Decoction." Also, "Waike Secret Records," Volume 3, contains "Elbow Reserve Ephedra Muscle Resolving Decoction," which has no cinnamon. It is commonly known by the ancients that ephedra resolves the muscles, so a separate record describes the uses of ephedra and includes the three characters "resolving the muscles." "Elbow Reserve" also has the name "Pueraria Lobata Branch Muscle Resolving Decoction." From this, it can be known that later generations' attribution of resolving the muscles exclusively to cinnamon twig, making empty arguments, is the saying of those with limited vision, sitting in a well and watching the sky.

Common Sense Question and Answer About Diseases 21

— Cheng Hanzhang

(38) Ascariasis and Enterobiasis (Pinworm Infection)

(Question) In what part of the human body do these two types of worms reside?

(Answer) They both reside in the intestines.

(Question) What does an ascarid (roundworm) look like?

(Answer) An ascarid looks very much like an earthworm. The male worm is 20 cm long, and the female worm is 40 cm long, with a diameter of 5 hao, and a light red color.

(Question) How does an ascarid infect the human body?

(Answer) It is caused by swallowing worm eggs attached to unclean water or vegetables. After the worm eggs enter the intestine, they hatch into larvae, which pass through the intestinal wall into the portal vein of the liver, reach the lungs, and then pass through the trachea into the esophagus and reach the small intestine, where they reside.

(Question) What do ascarid eggs look like?

(Answer) They are oval in shape, yellowish in color, with a two-layered eggshell with a rough and raised shell surface and particles inside.

(Question) What are the symptoms after an ascarid infestation?

(Answer) Sometimes there are no symptoms. Sometimes there is occult blood in the stool, or complaints of stomach pain on an empty stomach. Sometimes patients have symptoms of anemia or intestinal inflammation. When a large number of worms accumulate, the stool becomes constipated and the intestinal tract becomes blocked. Sometimes they invade the bile duct and cause jaundice, or form a liver abscess.

(Question) What is the treatment for ascariasis?

(Answer) Take santonin orally. The adult dose is 0.1-0.3 grams per day, for three consecutive days, and then take a laxative to expel them. The children's dose is 0.02-0.04 grams. In addition, sea wormwood can be used, 10-30 grams per day, decocted and taken orally for two or three consecutive days.

(Question) What do pinworms and their eggs look like?

(Answer) Pinworms are small, thread-like worms. The male worm is 4 hao long, and the female worm is 10 to 12 hao long. The eggs are bean-shaped, with a long diameter of 0.05 hao and a width of 0.02 hao.

(Question) What is the route of infection?

(Answer) After the worm eggs reach the stomach, they quickly develop and produce larvae, which gather in the small intestine and cecum. At maturity, they gradually migrate to the rectum. When the eggs mature, the female worms exit the anus and lay eggs near the anus.

(Question) What symptoms occur in people with enterobiasis (pinworm infection)?

(Answer) People infected with pinworms experience itching in the anal area, especially at night. Women experience itching in the vaginal area, or neurological symptoms caused by insomnia at night.

(Question) Why is enterobiasis difficult to cure completely?

(Answer) Because the worm eggs near the anus are scratched with fingers, and then transmitted to the mouth by the fingers, causing a second self-infection. This repeats endlessly, so it seems difficult to cure completely.

(Question) What is the method of prevention?

(Answer) To prevent self-infection, prohibit eating with your hands. Wear gloves or tie your hands at night.

(Question) What is the treatment for enterobiasis?

(Answer) First, apply gray-white ointment (i.e., mercury ointment) around the anus. Wash the intestines every week with 10% vinegar, or 100 to 300 times diluted quinine hydrochloride solution, 1000 times diluted tannic acid solution, or 200 times diluted salicylic acid solution. Take anthelmintics such as piperazine and santonin orally. It is advisable to take a laxative the night before taking the medicine to empty the intestines, which is more effective.

How to Remove Dust and Sand That Flies Into Your Eyes 22

— Translated by Wu Zhili

It often happens that dust or other foreign objects fly into our eyes, which is very troublesome. The pain can only stop after you think of removing it. The pain suffered and the large amount of tears shed can cause insomnia all night. If we do not find a way to remove it, inflammation will occur and even more troublesome eye problems will arise.

When coal ash enters the eye, do not close your eyes. Although it is difficult not to close your eyes, because closing your eyes is a quick reaction to protect your eyes, this closing of the eyes is very rapid and forceful, which will push the dust and sand deeper. So we have to close our eyes, or use our hands (clean hands, separate the upper and lower eyelids, and let the natural tears come out. At that time, the dust and sand may float out of the eye, or it can be dissolved in the acidity of the tears. After about a minute, then gently close your eyes. If you still feel something in your eye, you should straighten your head. Look down, pull the upper eyelid down, and pull it to the outside of the lower eyelid. In this position, you must automatically turn your eyeball upwards, and then let go, allowing the upper eyelid to return to its original position. Why do you do this? Because if the dust and sand are under the upper eyelid (the most common situation), the edge of the lower eyelid can grind and scrape out the dust and sand when the upper eyelid returns. If it doesn't work, you can try it several times.

If the method mentioned above does not work, we can know that this uninvited guest has probably run into the very thin cornea in front of the pupil. Once it gets to this place, you cannot move it yourself. All we should do is go to a doctor. Don't be cheap and go to a pharmacist or barber to relieve your troubles, because your eyes are too valuable. If you have a beautiful car, you will definitely not drive to the grocery market to show off, but instead you will get your car dirty. So you must not allow ignorant and inexperienced people to solve your pain.

Not only can coal ash be treated with the above methods, but also common ingrown eyelashes and iron filings entering the eyes, etc., can be cured in the same way. Many workers in foundry shops often do not take care or do not wear dust-proof glasses, so hot iron filings will come to their eyes. Although it hurts for a while, it doesn't hurt anymore, because the heat of the iron filings has burned the nerve endings on the cornea, but after a few hours, the severe pain will start again, and the tears will flow incessantly. This is because the nerve cells are regenerating, and therefore their transmission function is restored. In these shops, there is often a coworker who is confident that he can cure this eye disease. What does he do? He always carries a sharp small folding knife with him, specially for this purpose. He takes his treasured knife from his dirty bag with his muddy hands, and then tells the victim to open his eyes and not close them, until he has taken out the iron filings. Ordinary people's eyes cannot always be open and will always close, because the cornea is the thinnest and the most sensitive to stimuli. So when the tip of the knife touches her, the eyes will close in response. If this coworker and the victim are lucky, it will be taken out all at once, but usually it takes several times. After several times, the cornea will rupture. Once it ruptures, the danger of inflammation will come, because the knife is not disinfected. If inflammation occurs, the entire eye will enter a dangerous situation. The shallowest degree is ulceration, blurred vision and even blindness. So, dear coworkers! Don't let people mess with your precious eyes.

Not only workers have this danger, but we also have a high chance of getting iron filings in our eyes when we walk on the road. On the road, you may encounter iron-drilling craftsmen. Iron filings often fly from under his chisel into your eyes. Whenever two irons touch each other forcefully, hot iron filings will be produced. If there is no doctor nearby, if iron filings or other things get into your eyes, we can try to protect ourselves temporarily.

Page 20

If you have boric acid ointment or soft petroleum jelly (not saturated with carbonic acid), you can apply some to your eyes, and then close your eyes. Ointment has a lubricating function, which can prevent the cornea from being damaged by the friction of the iron filings inside. If you don't have the two medicines, you can put some castor oil, or olive oil, or vegetable oil in a small cup, and then boil it in boiling water for about a quarter of an hour (do not let the water splash into the oil). After the oil has completely cooled, please have someone slowly pour it into your eyes. It is best to use an eye dropper, followed by a disinfected (boiled) teaspoon. One or two drops is enough each time. Too much will irritate your eyes. Once the oil is in, you can close your eyes; it is best to keep both eyes fully open, because the movement of one eye will definitely affect the second eye. If there is an effect, there will be irritation.

So, friends, when you go out, it is best to always carry some boric acid ointment in an eye drop tube. In the event of an incident, use the tube to directly apply the medicine to your eyes. Do not use matches, toothpicks, or handkerchief corners to replace it. The most important thing is not to put eye stones or rapeseed in your eyes, hoping that she will move around inside and knock out the iron filings. For example, if we use a large bomb to blow up a small tree, although the tree is removed, everything around it will be lost. So you must strongly remember that when dust or iron filings get into your eyes, if the method I said at the beginning does not work, you should go to a doctor immediately, otherwise there is a risk of inflammation and even disability.

Headache Treatment 23

— Li Xing

Headache is a very common problem, so there are plenty of headache medicines on the market. When ordinary people have a headache, they go to buy headache medicine to relieve the pain. Few people ask why they have a headache. But now is the 20th century, an era of scientific prosperity, and medicine is advancing by leaps and bounds. We should use the knowledge of modern medicine to study and understand why we have a headache. We must know the cause of the headache in order to treat the headache fundamentally. Otherwise, taking headache medicine for a headache is just a perfunctory matter and not a fundamental solution. Taking headache medicine every time you have a headache, if you take too much, can also weaken your body. The latest medicine is to first find out the cause of the disease and then treat the symptoms accordingly, so it can be cured in all cases. This is the meaning of the rational treatment method in this article. The causes of headache are described below.

(A) Headaches are caused by toxins in the body. For example:

(1) When a person has a fever from illness, the body produces toxins, and the patient often has a headache.

(2) Toxins are produced spontaneously in the body, such as when the bowels are constipated. The large intestine absorbs toxins into the blood, so people with constipation often have a dull headache.

(3) There is an increase in waste products in the body due to imperfect kidney excretion function, so people with chronic nephritis often have headaches.

(4) Excessive cirrhosis of the liver or other diseases that damage the liver and hinder or reduce the liver's detoxification function also often cause headaches.

(5) Thyroid disease can also cause headaches.

(B) Headaches are caused by blood vessel diseases. For example:

(1) Heart fire. (2) Poor blood circulation. (3) High blood pressure. People with higher blood pressure and obesity often have headaches due to high blood pressure. (4) Hardening of the blood vessels in the elderly also often causes headaches. (5) Anemic people often have headaches due to insufficient blood in the brain. (6) Severe lung disease also causes headaches. (7) Syphilis. Old syphilis is especially called a headache.

(C) Headaches are caused by local diseases. For example:

(1) Eye strain, such as nearsightedness, farsightedness, astigmatism, and eye inflammation. Note: This is a particularly common cause of headaches. (2) Inflammation of the ear, nose, and throat. (3) Meningitis and neurological diseases. (4) Uterine diseases and uterine malposition.

Rational Treatment Method

From the above, in order to fundamentally solve a headache, you must first know the definite cause of the headache. These are described separately below.

Treat fever for headaches caused by fever. When the fever is cured, the headache will disappear.

For constipation, have a bowel movement every day. Method: Eat foods with more residue to make bowel movements easier every day. If you have a long-term constipation habit, you can take laxatives.

People with kidney disease should treat kidney disease. People with liver disease should treat liver disease. People with thyroid disease should also be treated.

If you have a habit of taking too much medicine, you must stop taking useless medicines.

If you have heart disease and heart inflammation, you must cure the heart disease. If the blood circulation is not smooth, make the blood flow smoothly.

High blood pressure must be treated to lower blood pressure, such as improving diet and helping excretion. When blood pressure is lowered, not only will the headache be gone, but the risk of stroke will also be gone.

For anemia, please ask a doctor to find out the cause of the anemia. First remove the cause of the anemia and then treat the anemia. When the anemia is cured, the headache will naturally disappear.

Headaches caused by lung disease must be treated for lung disease.

People with headaches who have had syphilis should not forget to be injected to treat syphilis.

Among the local causes, eye disease is the most important, and it also occupies an important position among all the causes. People with nearsightedness, farsightedness, and astigmatism use more eye strain than others when reading and doing fine work, so headaches occur. Wearing appropriate glasses can cure this type of headache. Students and people who use their eyes a lot must understand this pathology.

If headaches are caused by ear, nose, throat, or neurological diseases, the headache will be cured after removing the cause.

For women, if headaches are caused by uterine diseases or uterine malposition, curing the uterine disease or correcting the uterine position can eliminate the headache permanently.

Treatment of Pulmonary Cavities 24

— Ding Huikang

Combined Artificial Pneumothorax, Phrenic Nerve Resection, and Rib Resection

In our clinical practice, we often encounter patients with cavernous pulmonary tuberculosis in both lungs, whose treatment is the most difficult. Although sunlight, fresh air, nutrition, and rest are of great help in treating the lungs, they cannot exert their inherent functions in such cases. Symptomatic treatment, moreover, inevitably leads to the lament that medication is ineffective. Thus, we sit idly by as the patient's condition deteriorates day by day, groaning in bed. There is hardly a more miserable scene in life than this.

In ancient times, it was said that tuberculosis was certain death because there was no specific medicine to eradicate the tubercle bacilli. Although modern medicine is becoming more and more advanced, a specific medicine has not yet been discovered since the discovery of the tubercle bacilli. However, in sanatoriums, the treatment results for unilateral lung disease after various operations have been performed are quite astonishing. Although it cannot be said to be completely effective, severe cases are alleviated, mild cases are cured, hemoptysis is stopped, and high fever is eliminated. As for weight gain and reduction of sputum volume, they are even more common. Some cases relapse, either due to financial limitations and the inability to obtain sufficient treatment, or due to neglecting daily health maintenance. However, the overall results for unilateral pulmonary tuberculosis can be called excellent. However, there is still no excellent treatment method for bilateral pulmonary tuberculosis. Recently, at the Shanghai Tuberculosis Sanatorium, I have performed combined surgery on patients with cavities in both lungs. I will briefly describe it below.

A certain gentleman, 28 years old, was not in good general condition. He had had lung disease for more than three years, with a lot of coughing and phlegm. Tubercle bacilli were found in the sputum. On the X-ray, the upper half of the left lung was entirely shadowed, and bubbling sounds could be heard. An attempt at artificial pneumothorax was ineffective due to pleural adhesions. Therefore, phrenic nerve resection was performed first. However, this nerve resection did not have a superior effect in this case. However, it was performed to prevent danger before rib resection (i.e., complete cessation of work in the upper left lung), so the phrenic nerve resection was performed first to slightly elevate the left diaphragm to reduce the respiratory work of the left lung.

Then, I and the surgeon resected four ribs in a triangular shape from the back of the upper part of the left lung, narrow at the top and wide at the bottom. The affected part of the upper end of the left lung, which could not be compressed due to pleural adhesions, collapsed at this point.

At the same time, because a cavity was found in the upper part of the right lung, a small amount of artificial pneumothorax was performed two days before the rib resection, and it is still being continued. For more than two months now, all subjective and objective symptoms have improved a lot, and he is now going to the countryside for convalescence.

As for the prognosis, it is difficult to predict within this very short period of time. If proper recuperation and legal diagnosis and treatment can be obtained, there is still great hope for recovery. This depends on the patient's continued efforts. This surgical treatment is far better than the original medical treatment, which could only lead to waiting for death.

A Brief Discussion of Pulmonary Tuberculosis (20) 25

— Hu Jiayan

(5) Sputum: When coughing is mentioned, people usually think of excessive sputum. These two symptoms are almost like sisters. Although some people have only a dry cough and very little sputum. At the beginning of pulmonary tuberculosis, the amount of sputum is usually very small. It is purely mucous or mucoid and transparent. This sputum comes entirely from inflammation of the bronchial tubes, especially from the hilar glands. At this stage, the disease is mostly closed. However, even if tubercle bacilli are sometimes found in the sputum, it is not necessarily an exception. As the disease gradually progresses, the sputum is mostly mucopurulent, but the pus and mucus are not closely integrated, like in bronchitis and bronchiectasis. This kind of pus is mostly due to the formation of cavities in the lungs. It is originally very thin and fluid. When it passes upwards through the bronchial tubes and trachea, it is wrapped and aggregated by mucus, resulting in different forms such as linear, spherical, and coin-shaped. This is what we usually call spherical sputum and coin-shaped sputum. The pus produced in these cavities, in addition to mostly containing tubercle bacilli, also often contains other pyogenic bacteria, such as Staphylococcus aureus, Streptococcus, Tetradococcus, and Pneumococcus. In particular, the significance of Streptococcus in mixed infections is especially important.

(6) Hemoptysis: This is a symptom that makes people "turn pale at the mention of a tiger." Most patients, if they find that they have coughing and excessive sputum, and even that their bodies are thinner than before, regard it as insignificant and do not care at all. But if fresh blood streaks are found in the sputum, they mostly know that it cannot be delayed any longer, and will almost immediately go to a doctor to find a solution. This situation is very common in general society in our country. In fact, this is not entirely the case. We must know that examples of pulmonary tuberculosis causing direct life-threatening danger due to massive bleeding are very rare, far less than those of gastric ulcer and cirrhosis. Furthermore, hemoptysis does not necessarily occur when pulmonary tuberculosis is severe; it is also often found at the beginning of the disease. The prognosis of this kind of early hemoptysis is not necessarily bad. Sometimes, patients dare not be negligent because of this, and are happy to accept long-term recuperation and fundamental treatment, and do not regard the doctor's advice as trivial. As a result, they recover. In fact, there are many examples of this. Therefore, hemoptysis is undoubtedly a serious warning to patients. But I dare to say boldly that this warning is by no means unfounded, and is sometimes actually very beneficial.

Common Sense of Hygiene for Ears, Nose, Throat, and Eyes (Continued) 26

— Tang Renjin

(14) Nasal Polyps (commonly known as nasal fungus)

Nasal polyps (Maseupolyp, also known as mucous nasal polyp, Schleimpolypo) are what people generally call nasal fungus. It is a very common and important disease in nasal diseases. We also often encounter it in clinical practice. It is not a true tumor. It is simply a chronic inflammatory product. Its occurrence will never occur alone. There must be a causative disease as its origin before it can occur. The most common causative diseases are rhinitis and sinusitis (such as maxillary sinusitis and ethmoid sinusitis). This disease occurs most often in adults. It is very rare in children. Based on my more than ten years of clinical experience, I have never seen a child with nasal polyps. Nasal polyps mostly grow on the middle turbinate of the nasal cavity, or originate in the paranasal sinuses. Sometimes they grow in the nasopharynx, called choanal polyps. Nasal polyps often have thin stems, or broad bases. In the beginning, their shape is mostly spherical. If they grow larger later, they can become cystic, strip-shaped, or cockscomb-shaped. Their surface is very smooth. The color is grayish-white, or grayish-yellow, with a glassy luster. If a probe is used to test their hardness, they feel soft like jelly.

The main symptoms of this disease are nasal obstruction. Nasal breathing is impaired. Nasal secretions increase significantly, and are mucous or purulent. Patients often feel headaches and dizziness. After a long time, their spirits gradually decline. Memory often deteriorates. Patients sometimes suffer from sneezing. The nasal cavity often feels itchy. This is because the nasal polyps stimulate the nasal mucosa. Nasal polyps are prone to bleeding. Therefore, when a doctor examines them with a probe, or when a patient inserts a finger into the nostril and touches the nasal polyps, it can often cause nosebleeds.

The best and most appropriate treatment for this disease is to have a specialist explore its causative disease. Is it rhinitis or sinusitis? If the causative disease is sinusitis, then there is even more of a causal relationship. For example, if sinusitis is not treated for a long time, pus continuously flows out of its natural opening, and the mucosa is stimulated by the pus. At this time, it is very easy to develop chronic inflammatory products. These products are nasal polyps. On the one hand, the natural opening of the paranasal sinuses is narrowed by the newly formed nasal polyps. The natural function of pus drainage is also impaired. Sinusitis becomes even more severe. In this situation, surgery should be performed immediately. Use a cold snare (wire loop) to remove or strangle the nasal polyps. On the other hand, fundamental treatment of sinusitis should be carried out. Once cured, there will be no pus. Since the mucosa is not stimulated by pus, the recurrence of nasal polyps can naturally be avoided. People often say that nasal polyps will grow back even if they are cut off, so why bother cutting them off? This is all because the causative disease was not treated after the removal. Readers of this article may be able to explain this doubt.

Free Talk

The True Essence of Popular Language (Part 1) 27

— Li Jinxi

Regarding the term "popular language," please forgive my ignorance, I simply don't know what the differences or similarities are between it and "national language" or "vernacular"! However, things are not that simple, just interpreting it literally, it is indeed different from "national language" and "vernacular": "national language" is spoken in contrast to "foreign language," "vernacular" is spoken in contrast to "classical Chinese," "popular language" is spoken in contrast to "minority language"—language limited to a certain class (such as the so-called "comprador vernacular" or occupational use, etc.) or a certain place (such as dialects) can only be called "minority language." But "popular language" must also be limited to a certain era (such as the vernacular short stories of the Song and Yuan dynasties and the vernacular novels of the Ming and Qing dynasties, most of which were based on the "popular language" of the time, but now many not only cannot be spoken but also cannot be understood; today's "popular language" also advances with the years and changes with the times), and is limited to a certain country or a certain ethnic group (if "popular language" breaks through national boundaries, then it is "world language," which is not within the scope of this discussion). Then, the language that most people of a country and the entire nation can simultaneously understand and speak to each other is called "popular language." If the definition of "popular language" is indeed like this, then I still don't know what the differences or similarities are between it and "national language" or "vernacular."

However, things are still not that simple, all nouns have their own origins. Opening the material drawer of the China Dictionary Compilation Office, the noun "popular" has already existed in ancient times, and on the one hand is also an imported product. It can be used as a noun, or as an adjective, added to all other nouns, and thus "popular language" is produced from it. Forgive my verbosity! I will first pre-compile a long entry on "popular" for the dictionary (the original long draft was proposed by Mr. Wang Shuda, which was ultimately too "long," so only an excerpt is made here):

(1) In ancient usage, "popular" refers to a large group of peasants who were conscripted to serve as soldiers and workers. This is evidenced in the "Classics": "Book of Rites, Monthly Ordinances: "Early spring... do not gather the 'masses,' do not build city walls." (Zheng's note: "To prevent the beginning of farming." Song Zhangfu's explanation of the Monthly Ordinances: "Do not gather the masses, do not assemble large groups of apprentices; do not build city walls, do not undertake large-scale corvée labor.") "Early summer... do not start construction projects, do not dispatch the 'masses.'" (Zheng's note: "To prevent silkworm farming.") "Midwinter... do not build houses, and do not dispatch the 'masses.'" Also evidenced in the "Masters": Wu Zi (Wu Qi of the Warring States period) "Contingency: "Now there are few soldiers, who suddenly strike the gold and beat the drums on a narrow road, even if there are 'masses,' none will not be shocked." (This refers specifically to the large apprentice teachers during wartime.) Lü Shi Chunqiu, Summer Record of Sound and Music: "In the month of Zhonglu, do not gather the 'masses,' inspect and encourage agricultural affairs." Han Gao You's note: "Culu, April; 'masses' refers to military brigades and corvée labor," This is the official interpretation of the term "masses" in ancient times. Also evidenced in the "History": Book of Han, Biography of the Xiongnu: "When the Chanyu fled, his soldiers often mingled with the Han soldiers and followed the Chanyu. The Chanyu was unable to reunite with his 'masses' for a long time." (This also refers specifically to military brigades during wartime.) Therefore, the term "masses" was commonly used in ancient times, and its meaning was "large groups of peasant soldiers and peasant workers," but all were conscripted by those "above." (All previous dictionaries have missed the ancient meaning of this term: only Zhai Hao's Common Customs, Volume 8, Martial Arts category, has an entry on "masses," which also quotes a sentence from Guanzi, but is mistaken.)

(2) By the Middle Ages, the usage changed, and "masses" referred to monks, nuns, and lay Buddhists gathered together. This was a transliteration of the Indian "imported product." Originally, the Sanskrit word "Sangha" was translated as "community," with the meaning of harmony (originally just a "collective noun" of grammar, but the Buddhist world of the Tang and Song dynasties pointed out the number, such as the Lotus Sutra Xuanzan, according to the old meaning of the word "community," said "three people or more"; Tiantai Guanjing Shu said "four people or more, even hundreds of thousands of immeasurable"; Lotus Sutra Yishu added restrictions, saying "four great or more, up to twelve thousand people or less." A monk cannot be with the "Sangha", just as one cannot be called "community," as Ji Gui Zhuan 3 says: "One cannot say monk so-and-so, Sangha is Sangha, referring to the 'masses,' how can one tolerate one's own self, and immediately say four people? There is no such law in the West." But the customs of the Middle Kingdom are difficult to follow the Western law, so it is also said: "Distinguish as monks, the principle is also correct." Now the northern language often says, "Seven Communities chant scriptures," but calling one monk can also be called "one community," which is most common.) While "masses" are used to translate the Sanskrit word "Moha-Saingha", as in the Lotus Sutra, Introduction: "The World Honored One is in the 'masses', expounding the profound meaning of the Dharma." (The Treatise on Wisdom says: "The masses are all sages except for the Buddha." Originally limited to tonsured monks and nuns, but the Vimalakirti who entered the gate was a "layman," and "heavenly women" also became believers, so on this definition of "masses," the addition of "layman, female layman" is presumed to be acceptable.)

Talking About the Twenty-Five Dynastic Histories While Answering Mr. Lengmo 28

— Xia Gaizun

A few days ago, "Free Talk" published an article by Mr. Lengmo, entitled "Starting from the Twenty-Four Dynastic Histories," which mentioned the "Kaiming Edition Twenty-Five Dynastic Histories" currently being printed. He said that our method of printing this large thing into a small nine volumes, invisibly increased people's courage to read it; and said that the pricing of this book is also considered cheap, and its non-profit seeking is also commendable. After reading these words, we deeply appreciate his kind intention to praise us.

In addition, Mr. Lengmo seems not very supportive of our plan to reprint the entire history and sell the entire set. He advocates re-editing the entire history by category, selling it by category, to meet the needs of people who specialize in studying a certain aspect; he expressed many valuable opinions on classified re-editing. In our opinion, people who are interested in history will definitely express considerable agreement with his opinions.

We also had a plan for classified re-editing early on, and it can be said that it is roughly the same as Mr. Lengmo's opinion. There are two reasons why we are not implementing this plan first and reprinting the entire history first. First, we believe that in addition to people who specialize in studying a certain aspect, there are people who need to have the entire history by their side for reference at any time; and the libraries and school libraries in various places are established to meet the needs of people with different needs, and should especially have the entire history. Second, our method of printing this abridged version with specially cast zinc plates has a bit of an experimental meaning. If we are praised by everyone and the book sells, we will continue to walk this road and print other books; and the demand for the entire history seems to be larger, so we will reprint the entire history first as an experiment.

Our plan for classified re-editing is as follows: to collect the "books," "records," and "tables" of each history by category, so that each becomes a system. If the original book does not have these categories, such as the Records of the Three Kingdoms, we will try our best to adopt the things supplemented by later generations, such as Hong Liangji's Supplement to the Records of the Three Kingdoms' Territorial Records, Hong Yisun's Table of Officials of the Three Kingdoms, Hou Kang Yao Zhenzong's Supplement to the Records of the Three Kingdoms' Art and Literature, Wu Zengjin Yang Shoujing's Table of Counties of the Three Kingdoms, Zhou Jiayou's Table of Years of the Three Kingdoms, Zhou Mingtai's Table of Genealogy of the Three Kingdoms, etc. Even if the famous histories already have these categories, if later generations have made accurate supplements, such as Sun Xingyan's Supplementary Catalog and Textual Research of Sima Qian's Records of the Grand Historian, Heavenly Officials, Zhang Zongyuan Yao Zhenzong's Textual Research of the Book of Sui's Classics Records, etc., we will also try our best to adopt them. We not only want to compile the biographies of foreign countries, the biographies of the barbarians, the biographies of the Xiongnu, and the biographies of the Western Regions, etc., into special volumes, as Mr. Lengmo said; we also want to collect the biographies of the Confucian scholars and literary figures of various histories, so that they become a long series in academic history and literature; those figures who are listed in special biographies but have a great reputation in academic articles, such as Ouyang Xiu and Wang Anshi in the History of the Song Dynasty, we will also separately include their biographies. In this way, in Mr. Lengmo's view, he may have to say "that's what I had in mind!"

Finally, talking about the issue of low prices. Mr. Lengmo believes that if it is arranged, printed, and bound like the popular novels that are currently popular, the selling price seems to be even cheaper. In fact, this cannot be imitated. The sales of popular novels are calculated in hundreds of thousands or two hundred thousand, and when averaged out, the selling price can of course be extremely low. Our Twenty-Five Dynastic Histories will definitely not have that many sales. Moreover, we require the font to be clear and there to be no typos, so we use photographic zinc plate printing, and the ink and binding must also be quite particular: the cost increases, and the selling price naturally cannot be compared with popular novels. We believe that Mr. Lengmo can also understand this point.

He Buys a Shoe (Part 1) 29

— Cao Ming

After four o'clock in the afternoon in spring, Guangzhou puts on a soft and beautiful coat; Gaodi Road, lying at its southern end, is like a bright and charming necklace wrapped around colorful ornaments. On this road, those ornate shops selling silk fabrics, shoes, and various ornaments for women, shouting anxiously to attract customers, proudly boast, adding a lot of charming color to this hypocritical metropolis.

At the eastern end of Gaodi Road, on the left side, there is a "Lüheng" shoe store with a very shallow and narrow storefront and not very large scale. In the store, the chubby boss, whose face, eyes, mouth, and nose all have a consistent round shape, and who exudes a very shrewd spirit, is running back and forth in front of the right-angled counter, taking care of customers on the one hand, and directing the two young partners, one fat and one thin, on the other hand.

While four female students wearing the same neat and clean gray clothes and black skirts were meticulously and troublesomely pointing out the flaws in a pair of yellow fine beaded leather high heels to the boss, a soldier in his thirties, of medium height, wearing a tattered military uniform, and with a wooden leg clamped under his left arm, suddenly walked in. He stepped into the store, threw the wooden leg aside, and sat down on the long bench, shrinking himself as if to make himself smaller. His rough right hand pinched the thick, dirty hair upward, and his yellow-gleaming eyes, deeply hidden under thick eyebrows, stared at the female students on the opposite side, who opened their mouths as if frightened.

"A-Biao, ask that customer if he wants to buy anything?" the boss ordered unhappily, and then tried his best to use his smooth tongue to gently wash away the female customers' uneasiness.

"Rubber-soled shoes." The soldier, who had lost his left leg, answered the shop assistant, and turned his head to look at the diverse, flowing people on the road. The sharp and complex car horns and the sounds of conflict or harmony between people constituted a prosperous and noisy realm. In the milky and charming air, he seemed to rise from the chair. He carefully used his left hand to grab the excess left trouser leg, and the other hand caressed the knife scar in the middle of the black brush-like beard on his right cheek, deeply fearing that the turbid atmosphere of the city would insult his past achievements. He sighed, turned his face up flat, calm as if tidying up his fragmented mood; recalling the winter two years ago, how fiercely he fought with the Japanese soldiers in Wusong, and how he lost his left leg that night.

When the shop assistant handed him a pair of green canvas shoes, he picked up a shoe with a weary expression and examined it carefully, and finally tried it on his only foot.

"How much money?"

"Nine jiao a pair." The thin shop assistant answered listlessly, and after speaking, his eyes were fixed on the female students who were about to agree on a price.

Casual Literary Talks Outside the Door 30

— Hua Yu

(12) The End

We have said quite a lot already. In short, talking alone is not enough, what is important is doing. Many people need to do it: the masses and the pioneers; all kinds of people need to do it: educators, writers, linguists... This is already imperative, even if there is still a bit of going against the current at the moment, we can only pull and tow; it is certainly good to go with the flow, but we still have to steer the rudder.

Although this good method of pulling and towing or steering the rudder can also be discussed orally, it mostly benefits from experimentation. No matter how we look at the wind and water, the goal is only one: to move forward.

Everyone probably has their own opinions, now let me hear the high opinions of all of you. (The End)

Three Boards Two Supports 31

— TK

Younger Brother (13) 32

— Zhou Wen

I was taken aback, and when I looked, it turned out to be another colleague of my younger brother.

"Hey, don't make such jokes." My younger brother said sternly.

"Damn it, what joke are you making, let's go, let's play cards."

"You know I haven't been playing cards lately, I don't have any money." My younger brother's eyeballs were staring, and I thought he was going to get angry. Suddenly, a senior military officer in a gabardine military uniform flashed out at the street corner, and the colleague quickly turned his back, stood at attention, and saluted.

My younger brother pulled my sleeve and said:

"Let's go!"

We turned the corner at once, avoiding those two people. I really didn't expect that after only two years of not seeing each other, my younger brother had changed so much. Although his eyes were shining with innocence, his face was shrouded in silence. His military uniform was no longer particular, and the sloping belt he was using was now narrow.

"Younger brother, what about the belt I gave you?"

His face flushed slightly, and he replied:

"Hey, I don't want it anymore! So-so."

I stayed for two days, and he told me many indignant things. He still regretted not having read more books earlier, otherwise he could have left. He was very sad when he said this. When I was about to leave, he saw me off very far, grabbed my hand warmly, looked at me with wide eyes for a long time, and then sighed and said:

"Brother, I will definitely save some money, I will definitely come. I really don't want to do this kind of sacrifice!"

Tears welled up in his eyes, and I was also very sad. I walked far away from him, and still saw that he had not turned his head back. Oh, who knew, this time was actually a farewell forever!

It has already been several years since I came out again. I have learned many lessons from my wandering life. My younger brother, one year he couldn't come out, two years he couldn't come out, three years, and finally he sacrificed under the bullets!

Oh, sacrificed! What does it matter? But someone else is using binoculars on a high mountain and saying, "The First World War was just like this!" (The End)

Economic Supplement

Examination of Standards for Adulterated Cotton 33

— Zhu Xianfang

It is a widely acknowledged consensus that the adulteration of domestic cotton with water and other substances degrades its quality and hinders textile production. Strict measures must be taken to eliminate these practices and avoid unnecessary losses. Recognizing this, the government has formulated and promulgated regulations to address these issues. This action has long been sought by textile factories and technical organizations. The elimination of these long-standing malpractices and the imposition of severe penalties are undoubtedly justifiable. However, I have some reservations and wish to express my concerns regarding the first article, which stipulates that the statutory standard for domestic cotton is a water content of 11 percent. Furthermore, I would like to offer some clarifications on the eighth article, which limits the amount of foreign matter in raw cotton to 0.5 percent, a point that has been questioned and for which some have requested an increase.

Upon investigation, the legal moisture content standard for raw cotton in various European and American countries is 8.5 li long, equivalent to 7.83 percent of the total weight. This is because raw cotton, after being dried at a temperature of 220 to 230 degrees Fahrenheit, still absorbs 8.5 percent of its weight in moisture when exposed to the atmosphere. This is therefore taken as the standard for the statutory moisture content. Atmospheric humidity varies with time and location, and the natural moisture content of raw cotton also varies accordingly. Therefore, the standard moisture content must be adjusted based on the humidity of the location. It remains to be seen whether the statutory standard moisture content for raw cotton in our country can be based on the world's statutory standard moisture content of 8.5 li long, and whether the 11 percent statutory standard announced by the government is higher than the natural content. This must be determined by whether the average annual humidity in our country is significantly higher than the average annual humidity in Europe and America. A comparison of the average annual humidity in various European and American locations, as well as Osaka and Shanghai, is provided below:

Location　Average Humidity　Location　Average Humidity

New York　74%　Manchester　80%

San Francisco　86%　Paris　79%

Mumbai　78%　Osaka　74%

Berlin　76%　Shanghai　80%

Average over 34 years, as seen in the Chinese Yearbook of Commerce

European and American countries use 7.83% as the standard for moisture content in raw cotton. In Europe and America, San Francisco’s particularly high humidity does not lead to an increase in the moisture content standard for raw cotton, in order to avoid the standard content being lower than the natural content, which would cause losses to cotton farmers. Therefore, in our country, where the humidity is similar to that of Europe and America, it would not be impossible to use 7.83% as the statutory standard, as is done in Europe and America. However, the fact that we do not follow the same standard as other countries, and instead set the standard moisture content at 11 percent, which is 3.17 percent higher than in other countries, means that every 100 jin of raw cotton contains 3.17 jin more moisture than it should, leaving room for merchants to add moisture and causing textile factories to suffer a material loss of 3.17 jin. From a scientific standpoint, this cannot be considered appropriate, accurate, or as thorough as textile factories and technical organizations would like in terms of eliminating long-standing malpractices. Some may argue that the market used to accept 12 jin as the moisture content standard, so is it not reasonable to reduce it by 1 jin? Would setting the standard at 7.83 jin, as in other countries, be too far removed from reality and difficult to implement? However, customary practices can be broken. The lack of progress in our country's industries is often due to these hidden obstacles. Money changers profit from the lack of a unified currency system, exploiting exchange rates to the fullest extent. Cotton merchants profit from factories competing to buy raw cotton, bringing in moisture-laden cotton, with moisture levels as high as 12 jin or more. Over time, this has become customary, as if 12 jin is the market standard for moisture content. Just as changing "liang" to "yuan" was convenient, adopting a rational scientific viewpoint and revising the statutory moisture content standard for raw cotton to 7.83 jin would align our country's raw cotton with that of other countries, correcting international perceptions. Not only would domestic textile factories avoid unreasonable losses, but it would also greatly benefit the export of raw cotton. The current standard of 11 jin still allows merchants to add 3.17 jin of moisture, leading to many potential problems. The second article of the provisional regulations states, "The maximum limit for moisture content in domestic cotton sold in the market is 13 percent." The third article states, "The sale of domestic cotton with moisture content exceeding the maximum limit is strictly prohibited." This means that the market can allow the sale of raw cotton containing up to 13 jin of moisture per 100 jin, only deducting the water exceeding the statutory moisture content of 11 jin. In other words, it is permissible under national law to sell cotton with added water. How can this eradicate bad habits and prevent the degradation of cotton quality, thereby preventing people from hoping for improper gains? Furthermore, merchants can profit by mixing moisture-laden cotton without being detected by buyers, and their profits will likely fall within the legally permissible range. If merchants fully load up cotton with moisture, will textile factories not end up receiving domestic cotton containing 13 jin of moisture? Raw cotton with a moisture content of 13 jin will inevitably undergo chemical changes if stored for a long time, significantly affecting its strength and color. Ordinary Chinese cotton stored until April or May of the following year will inevitably be of lower color quality than when it was initially purchased. The strength of the finished product will also be inferior to that of products made from cotton that has not been stored for a long time. Cotton with excessive moisture content will, of course, rot. However, American and Indian cotton stored in the same location for one or two years will not change in color or strength when used, because the moisture content is purely natural, within 8.5 li jin, unlike domestic cotton, which is artificially moistened, exceeding the natural content by a large margin. The hindrance to textile production, the degradation of finished product quality, and the increased generation of recycled silk and recycled cotton have long been felt by those engaged in this industry as an immense pain. Will this not drive them to prefer using foreign cotton? The production of domestic cotton is currently insufficient to meet demand, and storing it for a year or two is still not unheard of. If production increases to the point where, as in the United States, it must be stored for many years before being sold gradually, and it still contains the statutory 11 jin of moisture, it will be impossible to prevent it from rotting and becoming unusable. Cotton farmers and cotton merchants will then suffer losses. Even if cotton with excessive moisture content is sold before it rots, its color and quality will have already decreased, and its price cannot be raised. This can also be seen as merchants shooting themselves in the foot. Some may also argue that if the statutory moisture content standard for raw cotton is lowered to 7.83%, as in other countries, the market price will not increase due to the deduction of moisture, and merchants will suffer losses. However, the price of goods varies depending on supply and demand. If demand exceeds supply, the price will be high, and it will be impossible to suppress it. If supply exceeds demand, the price will be low, and even if manipulators deliberately raise the price, it will be difficult to sustain. Therefore, the price of cotton has little to do with the statutory standard moisture content. If this argument is necessary, it is intended to grab more water in place of cotton to compensate for losses when cotton prices are low, or to add water to cotton to reduce its substance and compete for sales at a lower price when cotton prices are high. This kind of behavior of using water to match market prices is definitely not possible. Furthermore, cotton merchants buy cotton from cotton vendors, and cotton vendors buy cotton from cotton farmers. From cotton farmers to cotton vendors to cotton merchants, all buy and sell within the statutory standard moisture content, with no adulteration. What moisture needs to be deducted? How can one suffer losses due to moisture deduction? Therefore, with regard to the provisional regulations on eliminating adulteration with water, the statutory moisture content must be changed from 11 jin to 7.83 jin, and this must be implemented in the shortest possible time.

Foreign matter in raw cotton is inherently nonexistent in our country. When the cotton bolls open and the cotton fibers are exposed, cotton farmers patrol the fields and pick them by hand, with no opportunity for dead branches and fallen leaves to be mixed in. This is unlike the United States, where large-scale farming and mechanized harvesting make it difficult to avoid branches and leaves being mixed in. Therefore, domestic raw cotton is purer than Indian and American cotton. In addition to artificial adulteration, the only natural impurities are wind-blown dust and sand, which are minimal. Ginned cotton is clean cotton. Unless the ginning machine is defective, whole cotton seeds will not come out with the fibers, and broken seeds will not be mixed into the fibers. Therefore, the eighth article of the provisional regulations on eliminating adulteration, which limits foreign matter to 0.5 percent, will never be reached under natural conditions. Setting this as a publicly permitted amount inevitably raises concerns about artificial adulteration. How is any increase possible? Some commentators, without careful consideration, have requested that the sale of cotton with more than 2 percent impurities should be prohibited in the market, but there is no basis for this request in academic principles or facts. This needs to be corrected. These are my initial thoughts on the newly promulgated regulations, offered to the nation for discussion.

An Account Copied from Last Year's Customs Records 34

— Xinan

The economic situation of a country, whether prosperous or declining, should be known to its citizens. Knowing this, they can be alert to potential dangers and understand what needs to be avoided. However, a country's economic situation is complex and multifaceted. How can everyone be made aware of it? Therefore, there needs to be a simple report, such as customs records, for people to read, so that they can understand the general situation. However, some people find customs records to be voluminous and rarely read them. Recently, there has been a lot of attention paid to the export of silver, and people are urgently seeking measures to resist it, which is indeed an important task. However, if you look at the customs records, the export of silver is listed as a trade surplus and will be for the third year in a row! Why is it only being noticed now, instead of earlier? Isn't it too late? Fortunately, I am free and bored, so I will temporarily act as a "Teng Wen Gong," using the trade report published by the Customs in 1933 regarding the trade deficit and the inflow and outflow of gold and silver. To use a fashionable phrase, I will imitate Confucius's "transmit but not create" and extract information for the reference of readers:

"...Generally, when we look at China's huge trade deficit over the years, and the fact that silver is the only thing that can be used to offset it, we assume that raising the price of silver will reduce China's tangible trade deficit. However, upon closer analysis, we know that China is not a silver-producing country, so the silver it uses to offset the trade deficit must first be purchased from abroad. Therefore, what China urgently needs is to increase its ability to purchase silver. This shows that China's export prices must first be raised, or move in the same direction as silver prices, to be effective. However, at a time when China's silver production is declining and prices are falling, who would believe that raising the price of silver first would promote the use of silver in the East? I am afraid that the impact will encourage the import of foreign goods, and speculators will export silver to seek huge profits, leading to a potential outflow of silver from the country.

"Recently, China's import of silver has decreased due to the decline in export trade and the sharp drop in the prices of local products. By this year (1933), due to the principle of supply and demand, it has changed from a deficit to a surplus... "

"The amount of silver entering and leaving the country this year is extremely depressed, as can be seen in the following table of gold and silver imports and exports. The surplus even reached 14.4 million yuan. This surplus situation is not without precedent in Chinese trade history, as it was the case during the European War. At that time, the participating countries actively purchased silver in preparation for a prolonged war. As a result, silver prices soared, and exports increased sharply. As for this year, the United States abandoned the gold standard, and the value of Chinese silver dollars increased against the US dollar. Speculators competed to ship silver to the United States to seek huge profits, resulting in a large increase in the surplus. The import of silver from the United States this year was only worth 29.4 million yuan in national currency, while the export to that country reached 71 million yuan. It is clear that the US dollar is influencing the outflow of silver from China."

"Since the outbreak of the economic crisis, China's import of raw silver has been decreasing, which is undoubtedly a reflection of the domestic economic downturn. In view of the danger of raw silver outflow, the government stipulated that from April 6th of this year (1933), all exported silver bars, silver blocks, silver ingots, and other silver that can be used for coinage, except for Central Mint bars, will be subject to an export tax of 2.25% ad valorem to restrict it."

"China's ban on gold exports has been in effect since May 1930 and has not been relaxed to this day. The amount of gold exported with special permission from the government this year decreased by 39.9 million yuan compared to last year, as shown in the table below, while imports were roughly the same as last year. However, smuggling exports are certainly not small in number: not only can the number of seizures by customs be used as evidence, but also the huge export figures from Hong Kong below. Last year, Hong Kong officially imported gold worth HK$19.5 million and exported gold worth HK$63.7 million. This year, imports were only worth HK$6 million, while exports reached HK$88.9 million. Although the exact amount of gold transported from China to Hong Kong is unknown, it is certainly not insignificant. The following table compares the amount of gold and silver imports and exports and trade balance over the past ten years."

From the above three tables, we can see that: (1) Gold exports were banned long ago, and even if exports are allowed with special permission, they will still be exported, and there is no way to prevent them. (2) Silver was not exported in the early years for one reason: the world had no use for silver, so it was better to store it in silver-using countries like China. Now that silver has a destination, there is no reason why it would not be moved out. (3) Trade has not only been in deficit for the past ten years, but also in the past. For example, if we open a store, we import more goods from others than we export, and after settlement, we owe them money, which we ultimately have to pay in cash. Therefore, China only had a gold surplus in previous years (which can also be said to be expensive gold). Now that gold has been moved out in considerable amounts, even if the price of silver is not high, silver must also be moved out, especially since someone is buying silver.

Not only do we have to pay foreigners for the trade deficit, but we also have to pay foreigners for many other things. Let's list a few important ones:

(1) The principal and interest of indemnities for past defeats

(2) The principal and interest of foreign debts borrowed in the past

(3) The due profits and interest on investments in industrial and commercial enterprises

(4) Shipping costs

(5) Tuition fees for studying abroad

We only have expenditures, and they only have income: we will not discuss mutual exchanges for the time being (for a clear understanding of this situation, please refer to books on foreign exchange). As for the money that we Chinese can get from foreigners, it is shameful, fearful, and small:

(1) Foreign missionary expenses (mostly paid by the Chinese)

(2) Expenses for foreign troops stationed in China (they eat, use, and wear mostly their own things)

(3) Foreigners use the money they earn in China to invest in China. Although this is exploitation, fortunately there is this sum of money, otherwise the situation would be unimaginable.

We Chinese really shouldn't receive these few sums of money. And we have to pay foreigners so much money every year, which should have been unbearable long ago! In fact, it is not "bearable" now; it is like a bird's nest on a dangerous curtain! However, our country has another large source of income that can slightly offset the loss of foreign payments, which is the money earned by overseas Chinese through hard work. Although they are abroad, their hearts are in their homeland, and the amount of money they remit back every year is substantial. However, last year, the situation changed drastically. Let's look at what the customs records say:

"Xiamen: The trade balance has always relied on remittances from overseas Chinese to supplement it. In recent years, business in Southeast Asia has declined, and the economy of overseas Chinese has been extremely difficult. They have been returning to China in droves. The amount of money remitted back has been decreasing year by year, and the drop this year is especially large. According to estimates for this year, the amount of money remitted back this year has decreased from 40 million yuan in national currency last year to 30 million yuan..."

"Shantou... Many overseas Chinese have returned home, resulting in a large reduction in the amount of money remitted back this year. However, the exact amount of remittances is unknown due to a lack of statistics, but it is estimated to be no more than 25 million yuan."

"Jiangmen... Overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia have lost their jobs, and the anti-Chinese movement in Mexico is also very intense, resulting in a reduction of one-third in the remittances from overseas Chinese compared to last year. The huge trade deficit in this port cannot be offset, and commercial funds are very tight."

"Qiongzhou... The total value of cash and rice remitted back by overseas Chinese this year is 5 million yuan in national currency, which is said to be the total amount remitted back throughout the year!"

"Sheng Yue... In recent years, many Chinese workers in Burma have lost their jobs, and the amount of money remitted back has decreased sharply. There are not enough rupees in the market, and the exchange rate has increased."

With the above situation, the money that we Chinese rely on to pay foreigners is even more insignificant. As a result, the money owed to foreigners still has to be paid. May I ask, since the Chinese cannot use goods to offset it, what do they use to offset it? At present, there are many people discussing how to prevent the outflow of silver, but according to the situation recorded in the customs records, how can we reverse the inflow? Even if there is a solution, we should also know that a method that is beneficial to others may be harmful to others. Even if there are a hundred benefits and no drawbacks, we should also look at the environment. Don't benefit others while hurting yourself. Why make things difficult for your own people?

I am not speaking nonsense. There is no other way out except to be down-to-earth and help the industrialization effort. If there is, it is only a temporary solution. The so-called industrialization effort is to revitalize China's domestic industries in order to achieve self-sufficiency. Everyone should also thoroughly transform their "worship foreign" mentality. Don't value foreign goods and despise domestic goods; we should use domestic goods as much as possible. Domestic goods merchants should also not specialize in manufacturing domestic goods using foreign materials. They should quickly plan to switch to using domestic materials to live up to the name of domestic goods. At the same time, they should make efforts to pay close attention to quality and credit in all aspects and promote the export business. Then, there will naturally be a solution.

At present, we can only hope that the public will deeply remember to "save on foreign goods and use more domestic goods." With the public's determination, we can build a strong defense and perhaps be able to remedy the situation slightly.

The United States' Countermeasure to Nationalizing Silver 35

— Bo Di

Why does the price of silver tend to rise when the United States nationalizes silver? This is because the United States' nationalization order requires civilians to hand over all silver (except for a few minor exceptions) to the mint within three months. The mint deducts 61.32% of the value as a coinage profit, and the remaining amount is paid to the silver seller at a price of 50.1 cents per ounce. This payment of 50.1 cents per ounce is not far from the current price of silver. However, the Silver Purchase Act of 1934 (the nationalization order is based on this law) stipulates that one silver dollar certificate should be issued for every ounce of silver received. The silver nationalization order also stipulates that "the silver certificate shall maintain a full silver reserve... when redemption is requested, it will be exchanged for standard U.S. dollars." This means that the silver initially purchased at a price of 50.1 cents per ounce will be worth $1.29 when used as a reserve to issue banknotes. In other words, one ounce of silver, initially worth 50.1 cents, will then be worth $1.29 without any discount. This is more than double the price of silver.

Under such circumstances, speculation is naturally triggered, and in China, it naturally induces inequality in the price level between Chinese and foreign silver, leading to the outflow of silver. What are the consequences of the outflow of silver?

First, the emptiness of cash reserves. China adopts a decentralized issuance system for banknotes, meaning that not only the central bank can issue banknotes, but also many other banks issue banknotes. This is different from advanced countries that adopt a centralized issuance system. However, the issuance reserve system of advanced countries that adopt a centralized issuance system generally adopts a system of 40% cash reserve and 60% guarantee reserve; while China is exactly the opposite, with 60% cash reserve and 40% guarantee reserve. Therefore, excessive outflow of silver will inevitably affect the 60% cash reserve. Since cash reserves are reduced, the amount of banknotes in direct proportion to it will also be reduced, creating a phenomenon of deflation. At that time, prices will fall, and the economic downturn will be even worse.

Second, the disillusionment of the new silver standard currency. According to Article 11 of the Regulations for the Minting of Silver Standard Currency, the minting of China's new silver coins stipulates that "for silver with a fineness of 999 per thousand, each yuan shall contain 23.493448 grams of pure silver, plus a minting fee of 2.25% of one yuan." This means that the nominal value of one yuan of the new silver standard currency is 2.25% higher than its actual value. This 2.25% is the government's profit in the name of coinage difference, so the government's coinage revenue is about 90,000 yuan per month, with a minting volume of 4 million. So why are civilians willing to pay 2.25% to send silver to the mint to mint new silver dollars? This is because foreign countries are dumping silver in China, and the price of silver in China is higher than that in foreign countries. Therefore, instead of spending freight, insurance, packaging fees, etc. to transport Chinese silver to foreign countries for sale, it is better to pay this 3.25% to mint silver dollars in the country nearby. However, now, as a result of the United States raising the price of silver, the price of silver in foreign countries is higher than that in China. Therefore, instead of paying 2.25% to mint silver dollars, it is better to pay freight and insurance to sell them to foreign countries. As a result, not only will the number of newly minted silver dollars gradually decrease, but even the silver dollars that have already been minted may gradually be transported to foreign countries; thus forming the disillusionment of the new silver dollar currency, and the government losing a batch of coinage revenue every day, which is secondary.

Regardless of whether the silver policy has much basis in academic theory (I have commented on this point in the 17th issue of the second volume of New China), this kind of impact on China is possible. So, what countermeasures should we have? Regarding this point, contemporary scholars have discussed it for a long time, but there is no perfect solution. In principle, I agree with Mr. Yin Pu's opinion that to stabilize the domestic currency position, it is necessary to break away from the relationship with foreign banks, but in terms of practical procedures, the "remittances cannot be cashed" method may not be permitted by foreign commercial banks, so we have to find another appropriate solution.

In my opinion, although silver is a commodity in the world, it is a currency in China; but currency has two functions, internal and external. For example, in countries that implement the gold standard, gold is a guarantee means within the country and can actually circulate, while externally it is a means of circulation and a method for settling international trade. It can be seen that silver in China, as a currency, still maintains the appearance of a free silver standard system. It is not only a means of circulation externally, but also a guarantee means internally, and at the same time a means of circulation. Therefore, it can be freely bought and sold, freely minted, and freely exchanged for cash, and freely enter and exit. Under such a free silver standard system, it is impossible to separate China's currency from the world silver price. To separate the value of China's currency from the world silver price, we must stop China's unlimited silver standard system and make it a "limited silver standard system"; this is the best method, which is to make silver only a guarantee means domestically and a means of circulation externally. In other words, stop cashing domestically, but do not prohibit silver exports externally; however, stopping cashing is often equal to prohibiting silver exports. Because stopping cashing makes it impossible to obtain silver for export; in this way, the method of repaying the value of imports will be exhausted. To remedy this point, the central bank may be ordered to buy and sell raw silver at exchange banks (such as the Bank of China); however, when civilians want to purchase silver from the central bank for export to pay for goods, they must be required to submit import certificates for the goods, etc., to show restrictions. In this way, China's silver is also equivalent to being nationalized.

However, before implementing this nationalization policy, China must improve its banknote issuance system. China must change its decentralized issuance system into a sound centralized issuance system, and the 60% cash reserve system may also be changed to 40%. Because centralized issuance means centralized reserves, which makes it easier to implement control, and reducing the cash reserve can save silver and strengthen the role of silver as a guarantee means.

With such measures, even if the price of silver continues to rise, our China can be less affected by it.

Commercial News 36

Finance

The Foreign Exchange Market Was Quiet on Sunday

Yesterday was Sunday, and banks were closed as usual, which made the market even quieter. The foreign exchange interbank offered rate in the market was 9 points in both the morning and afternoon sessions, a further decrease of 1 point compared to the previous day. In terms of settlements, due to the bank holiday, everything was completely suspended, with only transactions between money shops themselves. The total amount of foreign exchange settlements was over 29 million, and the amount of remittances from various places was over 200,000. In terms of interbank lending, the morning session saw 3.1 million in transfers and new transactions, the afternoon session saw 300,000 in transactions, the Small General Association saw 300,000 in transactions, and pawn transactions saw over 400,000 in redemptions and 200,000 in new transactions. The situation in the subsidiary currency market was still stable. Although the Jiangnan small dollars once fell slightly in the morning session, trading at 832.8 yuan, they still returned to 833 yuan in the afternoon session, so the result was still the same as the previous day. The volume of transactions was 3,000 jiao in the morning session and 5,000 jiao in the afternoon session. Guangdong small dollars had slight fluctuations, trading at 748.8 yuan in the morning session and 749.3 yuan in the afternoon session. As a result, they rose by 1.3 yuan compared to the previous day. The volume of transactions was 90,000 jiao in the morning session and 5,000 jiao in the afternoon session. Copper coins also did not fluctuate, remaining at 317,000 wen, with a transaction price of 125,000 yuan, equivalent to 40,645 strings of wen.
